Scriptural Proofs for the Grave Questioning
Provides the scriptural and consensual basis for the grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the belief in the grave questioning is established through mutawatir hadith and unanimous consensus of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
Certainty in unseen matters comes from multiple, mutually reinforcing chains of narration.

How do we know the grave questioning is real? The author explains that the hadith on this topic have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission), leading to consensus. Two key hadiths are cited to demonstrate this.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of tawatur
Read how the author says many hadiths in their totality reach tawatur. This means they are undeniably authentic.
Tawatur is the strongest form of hadith authentication.
2
Read the first hadith from the eclipse prayer
This hadith from Bukhari and Muslim reports the Prophet's description of the grave trial. Note the answers of the believer and hypocrite.
3
Read the second hadith about the two angels
This hadith gives more detail: the angels make the deceased sit up and ask about Muhammad. The believer's response leads to Paradise.
Both hadiths confirm the same reality.
4
Connect to consensus
The author states that all Muslims have agreed on this belief. Why does consensus matter in Islamic theology?
Consensus is a source of certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - سؤال القبر :
فإذا مات الإنسان ، أرسل الله إليه ملكين بشكل مفزع مخيف ، فسألاه عن الدين الذي عاش عليه وعن علمه بهذا الرجل الذي سمع عنه ، وهو محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، فمن كان قد ثبته الله عز وجل بالقول الثابت ، ومات على الحق وختم له بالحسنى ، ألهمه الله الجواب على سؤال الملكين ، دون أن يعروه شيء من مظهرهما المخيف ، ومن لم يكن معتصماً بحبل الإيمان في حياته الدنيا ، ومات على ماعاش عليه من لهو وعصيان وإدبار عن الحق ، ملأ الله قلبه فزعاً منها ، فغاب عن فكره الجواب المطلوب ولم يحر جواباً على ما يقولان

عبد
B - The Question of the Grave:
When a person dies, God sends to him two angels in a terrifying, frightening form, and they ask him about the religion he lived upon and about his knowledge of this man he heard about, namely Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. Whoever God has made firm with the firm word, died upon the truth, and was sealed with goodness, God inspires him with the answer to the two angels' question, without being affected by anything of their terrifying appearance. And whoever was not clinging to the rope of faith in his worldly life, died upon what he lived upon of amusement, disobedience, and turning away from the truth, God fills his heart with terror from them, so the required answer disappears from his mind and he gives no answer to what they say.
These are among the unseen realities that no one perceives except one who has reached that fate, and each of us is about to reach it. Many authentic hadiths, which in their totality reach the level of tawatur, have indicated them. Therefore, all Muslims have reached consensus on believing in that according to what the certain report indicates.
Among the hadiths reported in that regard is what al-Bukhari and Muslim and others narrated: that the Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace, once led the people in the eclipse prayer, then stood up, praised God, and then said: 'There is nothing I had not seen that I did not see in this place of mine, even Paradise and Hell. And it has been revealed to me that you will be tried in the graves like or close to the trial of the Dajjal. One of you will be brought and it will be said to him: "What is your knowledge of this man?" As for the believer or the certain one—a variation by the narrators—he says: "He is Muhammad, the Messenger of God; he brought us clear proofs and guidance, so we responded, believed, and followed." It will be said to him: "Sleep in peace; we knew you were a believer." As for the hypocrite or the doubter—also a variation—he says: "I do not know, I heard the people saying something and I said it."
That is what the two Shaykhs narrated with their chains that the Prophet said: 'When the servant is placed in his grave and his companions depart, and he indeed hears the sound of their sandals, two angels come to him, make him sit up, and say to him: "What did you used to say about this man?" As for the believer, he says: "I bear witness that he is God's servant and His messenger." He said: It will be said to him: "Look at your seat in Hell; it has been replaced for you with a seat in Paradise."'
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation of the trial of the grave (fitnat al-qabr). It begins by describing that after death, God sends two terrifying angels who ask the deceased about his religion and about the Prophet Muhammad. For those whom God has made firm (al-qawl al-thabit), they are inspired with the correct answer and are not frightened by the angels' appearance. For those who lived in sin and disbelief, their hearts are filled with terror and they fail to answer. The author emphasizes that this is an unseen reality (haqiqa ghaybiyya) that each person will experience. The passage then notes that many authentic hadiths, reaching the level of tawatur (indisputable mass transmission), support this, leading to unanimous consensus (ijma') among Muslims. Two hadiths are cited: the first from Bukhari and Muslim about the eclipse prayer and the trial of the grave, where the Prophet describes the questioning and the answers of the believer and the hypocrite; the second is also from Bukhari and Muslim (al-Shaykhan) describing the two angels who make the deceased sit up and ask about the Prophet, and the believer's response leads to his seat in Hell being replaced with Paradise. The passage thus grounds the belief in the grave questioning in scriptural sources and consensus.

Key Terms
التواتر
الإجماع
الخبر اليقيني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in the grave questioning has no solid proof.
Correction: It is based on many authentic hadiths reaching tawatur and unanimous consensus.

Checkpoint
What type of hadith evidence supports the grave questioning according to the passage?
A) A single authentic hadith
B) Many authentic hadiths that reach the level of tawatur
C) Weak hadiths accepted by analogy
D) Only rational proof

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a certain belief because it is supported by mutawatir hadith and the consensus of the Muslim community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the grave questioning is as certain as this lesson claims, how would you answer the angels' question about 'this man' right now? Not based on your upbringing or what people say, but on your own conviction—would your answer be 'I know he is the Messenger of God' or 'I don't know, I just said what others said'? And what does your daily life reveal about your actual belief?
?
The Prophet compared the grave trial to the trial of the Dajjal. Are you preparing for that moment with the same urgency as you would prepare for a physical trial? What concrete step can you take before the day ends to strengthen your knowledge of Muhammad and his message so that your answer in the grave is one of certainty?
?
You will experience the grave questioning alone. No one will answer for you. If you were to die tonight, would you face the angels with confidence or with hesitation? What is the one thing you need to change or learn so that you can say 'I bear witness that he is God's servant and messenger' with absolute sincerity?

Universality of Grave Questioning (Answer to an Objection)
Author proves grave questioning applies to all dead, answers objection, quotes Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the questioning in the grave applies to all deceased, regardless of burial, and how the answer to the objection relies on the principle of possibility and the unseen nature of spiritual realities.

Core Idea
Grave questioning is universal; Allah can restore life to any particles, wherever they are.

In this passage, the author establishes that the questioning in the grave is not limited to those physically buried. He addresses a common objection: how can questioning occur if the body is destroyed? The answer lies in understanding that what is possible for Allah includes restoring life to scattered particles, and that the afterlife belongs to a different order of existence, beyond physical perception. The author supports this with a quotation from Imam al-Ghazali.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
First, read the Arabic passage aloud if possible, then the translation. Notice the author's argumentative style: he states the evidence, clarifies a point, raises an objection, and replies.
Pay attention to the phrase 'تغليباً' (by predominance) – it's key to understanding why the grave is mentioned.
2
Identify the objection and answer
Locate the objection (فإن قلت) and the answer (والجواب). The objection questions how questioning can happen if the body is destroyed. The answer invokes the category of the possible (الممكنات) and distinguishes between what is impossible and what is merely unfamiliar.
Notice the author's use of 'غاية الأمر' to indicate the core of the answer.
3
Analyze the principle of possibility
The author argues that the matter falls within the realm of possibilities (الممكنات). Reflect on the distinction between something being logically impossible (مستحيل) and something being possible but unfamiliar (ممكن غير مألوف). The author gives examples of scattered particles.
This principle is central to rational theology (ilm al-kalam) – nothing is impossible for Allah except logical contradictions.
4
Examine the Ghazali quote
The author quotes Imam al-Ghazali to support the answer. Ghazali argues that the physical eye is not suited for perceiving the malakut (celestial realm), just as the Companions believed in Jibril without seeing him. This reinforces that the dead can perceive angels without physical sight.
Consider the analogy: if you accept that the Prophet saw Jibril while others did not, why not accept that the dead see angels in a different state?
5
Connect to the key takeaway
The passage concludes that questioning is universal for all deceased. The ascription to the grave is by predominance, not exclusivity. The key is that Allah can restore life to any particles, and the afterlife operates on a different order.
This resolves the common misunderstanding that only buried people experience grave questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا هو دليل التواتر الذي لا يقبل الريب أو الاحتمال. ثم إن إسناد السؤال إلى القبر جار على وجه التغليب إذ غالب من يموتون يدفنون في القبور، فيكون سؤال الملكين بالنسبة إليهم في القبر بعد أن يتولى عنهم أصحابهم كما قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. فأسند السؤال إلى القبر تغليباً. وإلا فلا جرم أنه شيء ثابت بالنسبة لكل من مات سواء دفن في القبر أم غرق في البحر أم أكلته السباع أم التهمته النيران. فإن قلت: ولكن كيف يتم السؤال والجواب رغم موته في هذه الأحوال كلها؟ والجواب أن الأمر داخل في حيز الممكنات، وليس من قبيل المستحيلات. غاية الأمر أن من الممكنات أموراً لم نشاهدها ولم نتعود على تصورها وهضم كيفيتها، ومنها ما ذللته المشاهدة والرؤية المستمرة، فيتخيل الإنسان لأول وهلة أن الأول مستحيل والثاني وحده الممكن. فليس عسيراً على الله جل جلاله أن يعكس الحياة مرة أخرى على ذرات الجسم سواء كانت مجتمعة في قبر، أم موزعة في فلاة أم متفرقة في بطن سبع، بذلك السؤال والجواب، ويرى الملك الذي يسأله ويكلمه. وليس ثمة مطمع في أن تعلم كيفية ذلك تحليلاً، إذ إن حقائق ما بعد الموت متعلقة بنظام آخر مختلف كل الاختلاف عن نظام هذا العالم المرئي للأحياء، ولننقل لك في بيان هذه المسألة ما يقوله الإمام الغزالي رحمه الله: إن هذه العين لا تصلح لمشاهدة الأمور الملكوتية، وكل ما يتعلق بالآخرة فهو من عالم الملكوت. أما ترى الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كيف كانوا يؤمنون بنزول جبريل، وما كانوا يشاهدونه، ويؤمنون بأنه عليه السلام يشاهده. فإن كنت لا تؤمن بهذا فتصحيح أصل الإيمان بالملائكة والوحي أهم عليك، وإن كنت آمنت به وجوزت أنه يشاهد النبي مالا تشاهده الأمة فكيف لا تجوز هذا في الميت؟
This is the evidence of tawatur (تواتر) that does not admit doubt or possibility. Then indeed, ascribing the questioning to the grave is done by way of predominance, since most of those who die are buried in graves. So the questioning of the two angels is with respect to them in the grave after their relatives have taken charge of them, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) said. So the questioning was ascribed to the grave by way of predominance. Otherwise, there is no doubt that it is a matter established for everyone who dies, whether buried in the grave, or drowned in the sea, or eaten by beasts, or consumed by fire. If you say: But how does the questioning and answer take place despite his death in all these cases? The answer is that the matter falls within the realm of possibilities (mumkinat), not impossibilities. The only thing is that among possibilities there are things we have not witnessed and are not accustomed to conceiving and digesting their modality, and among them are things that constant observation and sight have tamed. So a person imagines at first glance that the first is impossible and the second alone is possible. So it is not difficult for Allah, Exalted is His Majesty, to restore life again to the particles of the body, whether they are gathered in a grave, or scattered in a desert, or dispersed in the stomach of a predator, for that questioning and answer, and he sees the angel who questions him and speaks to him. And there is no hope of knowing the modality of that through analysis, for the realities of the afterlife are related to another system completely different from the system of this visible world of the living. And we will convey to you in explaining this matter what Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) says: 'Indeed, this eye is not fit for observing the malakut (ملكوت) matters, and everything related to the afterlife is from the world of malakut. Do you not see the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, how they believed in the descent of Jibril, and they did not see him, and they believed that he (peace be upon him) saw him? If you do not believe in this, then correcting the foundation of belief in the angels and revelation is more important for you. And if you believe in it and allow that he sees the Prophet what the ummah does not see, then how do you not allow this in the case of the dead?'
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The author first asserts that the established truth about the questioning in the grave applies to all dead, regardless of burial. He clarifies that ascribing the questioning to the grave is by predominance, not exclusivity. He then raises an objection: how can questioning occur if the body is destroyed by drowning, predators, or fire? The answer relies on the principle of possibility (mumkinat): what is possible for Allah includes restoring life to the particles wherever they are. The author distinguishes between what is impossible and what is merely unfamiliar, and he supports his answer by quoting Imam al-Ghazali, who argues that the physical eye cannot perceive spiritual realities, just as the Companions believed in Jibril without seeing him. Thus, the dead can see and hear the angels through a different order of existence.

Key Terms
التواتر
السؤال في القبر
الممكنات
الملكوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only those physically buried in a grave experience the questioning in the grave.
Correction: The questioning is universal for all deceased; the ascription to the grave is by predominance because most are buried, but Allah can restore life to any particles.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the questioning in the grave applies to all dead, not only the buried?
A) Because the hadith explicitly says so.
B) Because the angels go to every dead person regardless of location.
C) Because the ascription to the grave is by predominance and Allah can restore life to any particles.
D) Because the questioning happens before death.

Key Takeaway
The questioning in the grave applies to all deceased, because Allah can restore life to any part of the body and the afterlife belongs to a different order of existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight and your body were scattered or consumed, do you truly believe you will still be questioned? What does your current daily preparation (or lack thereof) reveal about that belief?
?
The author says the afterlife belongs to a completely different system. In what ways do you live as if this world's system is the only reality? What would change today if you fully internalized that another system awaits you?
?
Ghazali asks: if you believe the Companions believed in Jibril without seeing him, how can you deny the dead perceiving angels? Are you comfortable with trusting the unseen on matters of the grave, or do you demand evidence that suits this world? What does your answer say about your iman?

Evidence for Punishment and Bliss of the Grave
Author introduces the reality of grave punishment and bliss, citing Quranic verses as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment and bliss of the grave are proven by certain mutawatir reports, particularly Quranic verses, and how the author addresses potential objections.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is an unseen reality proven by certain reports, not reason.

In this passage, the author introduces a new topic: the punishment and bliss of the grave. He immediately establishes that these are unseen realities that can only be known through certain transmitted reports (khabr yaqini mutawatir). As a sample of such evidence, he cites two Quranic verses that describe the anguish of death for wrongdoers. He then addresses a potential objection: the verses speak about the moment of death, not the grave. He argues that this does not weaken the evidence, because the death experience is part of the broader reality of afterlife punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the author's method: he states a principle, then provides evidence.
The author calls these 'unseen realities' (حقائق غيبية) which require special evidence.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Locate the two Quranic citations. Understand the context of each: Surah Al-An'am 6:93 and Surah Muhammad 47:27. Both describe the angels striking the wrongdoers at death.
3
Understand the objection and response
The author anticipates that someone might say these verses are about death, not the grave. His response is that this does not damage the proof because the death experience is connected to grave punishment.
The footnote refers to al-Ghazali's Ihya' for further discussion.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is it important that the author starts with the claim that these are unseen realities? This sets the epistemological framework: we rely on revelation, not reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج - عذاب القبر ونعيمه : وهما من الحقائق الغيبية التي ثبت الدليل عليها أيضاً بالخبر اليقيني المتواتر. ولنذكر لك طائفة من هذه الأخبار، إذ هي العمدة في موقفنا من المغيبات التي لا مجال للمشاهدة والعقل في الخوض فيها. 1 - يقول الله تعالى: ( ولو ترى إذ الظالمون في غمرات الموت والملائكة باسطوا أيديهم أخرجوا أنفسكم، اليوم تجزون عذاب الهون ) [الأنعام: 93]. ومثله قوله تعالى: ( فكيف إذا توفتهم الملائكة يضربون وجوههم وأدبارهم ) [محمد: 27]. ولا يخدش في دلالة الآيتين على ما نقول، أن العذاب كائن - في (1) إحياء علوم الدين: 4-500
C - Punishment and Bliss of the Grave: Both are among the unseen realities whose evidence has been established also by certain (يقيني) mutawatir report. And we will mention for you a group of these reports, for they are the mainstay in our position regarding the unseen matters for which there is no room for observation and intellect to delve into. 1 - Allah the Exalted says: 'And if you could see when the wrongdoers are in the agonies of death and the angels extend their hands, "Discharge your souls! Today you will be awarded the punishment of humiliation."' [Al-An'am: 93]. And similar is His saying: 'Then how will it be when the angels take them in death, striking their faces and their backs?' [Muhammad: 27]. And the fact that the punishment occurs at [the time of death] does not mar the indication of the two verses regarding what we say, that the punishment is – in (1) Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din: 4-500.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section on the punishment and bliss of the grave. The author declares that both are unseen realities proven by certain mutawatir (متواتر) reports. He then begins listing these reports, starting with two Quranic verses. The first verse (Quran 6:93) describes the agony of death for wrongdoers, with angels striking them. The second verse (Quran 47:27) similarly describes angels striking faces and backs at death. The author preemptively notes that these verses describe punishment at death, not specifically in the grave, but he argues that this does not detract from their proof of grave punishment, because the death experience is part of the broader reality of the afterlife. The passage ends with a footnote reference to al-Ghazali's Ihya'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think Quranic verses that describe punishment at death have no bearing on the reality of grave punishment.
Correction: The author argues that these verses are in fact evidence for grave punishment, because the punishment begins at death and continues in the grave.

Checkpoint
What type of evidence does the author state supports the reality of grave punishment and bliss?
A) Rational proofs alone.
B) Quranic verses only.
C) Certain mutawatir reports, which include Quranic verses.
D) Consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the grave are proven by certain mutawatir reports, including Quranic verses that describe punishment at death, which the author argues are valid evidence despite occurring at death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verses describe the agony of death and the angels striking the wrongdoers. If you were in that moment, what would you wish you had done differently? Write one concrete action you will take today to prepare for that hour.
?
The author emphasizes that these unseen realities are known only through reports, not reason. Where in your life do you rely more on your own reasoning than on what Allah and His Messenger have told you? Are you willing to submit even when you cannot see?
?
Imagine you are the one being told 'Discharge your souls!' because of your own wrongdoings. Does that thought change how you treat others today? What is one relationship you need to mend before death arrives?

Unseen Matters

The Reality of Resurrection and the Unseen Grave
Al-Buti argues for the reality of resurrection and the unseen nature of the grave's questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the events of the grave and resurrection must be accepted as unseen realities beyond scientific analysis, based on the same principle that underlies belief in angels and revelation.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen grave follows the same logic as belief in angels.

This lesson tackles a common doubt: how can we believe in events like resurrection and the questioning in the grave if we cannot perceive them? Al-Buti explains that Allah can easily restore life, but the deeper point is that these realities belong to a completely different order—the malakut (angelic realm). He quotes Imam al-Ghazali, who argues that the physical eye is not suited for such matters, just as the Companions believed in Jibril's descent without seeing him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the main claim: Allah can restore life, and the deceased experiences question and answer with an angel.
Pay attention to how al-Buti shifts from the physical possibility to the epistemological barrier.
2
Identify the epistemological argument
Al-Buti says 'there is no hope in knowing how that is analytically.' He argues that the afterlife follows a completely different system from the visible world. This is a key point.
Why is analysis impossible? Because the afterlife is not part of this worldly system.
3
Analyze al-Ghazali's analogy
Al-Ghazali says the eye is not fit for malakut. He uses the Companions as an example: they believed the Prophet saw Jibril without seeing him themselves. If you accept that, you should accept that the deceased sees the angel.
The analogy links belief in unseen grave events to belief in revelation itself.
4
Reflect on the principle
The underlying principle is that we must accept unseen realities when confirmed by revelation. This is not blind faith but a rational extension of our belief in the unseen aspects of Islam.
Consider: if you deny the grave's events, you might undermine your belief in angels and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فليس عسيراً على الله جل جلاله أن يعكس الحياة مرة أخرى على ذرات الجسم سواء كانت مجتمعة في قبر، أم موزعة في فلاة أم متفرقة في بطن سبع بذلك السؤال والجواب، ويرى الملك الذي يسأله ويكلمه. وليس ثمة مطمع في أن تعلم كيفية ذلك تحليلاً، إذ إن حقائق ما بعد الموت متعلقة بنظام آخر مختلف كل الاختلاف عن نظام هذا العالم المرئي للأحياء، ولننقل لك في بيان هذه المسألة ما يقوله الإمام الغزالي رحمه الله: إن هذه العين لا تصلح لمشاهدة الأمور الملكوتية، وكل ما يتعلق بالآخرة فهو من عالم الملكوت. أما ترى الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كيف كانوا يؤمنون بنزول جبريل، وما كانوا يشاهدونه، ويؤمنون بأنه عليه السلام يشاهده. فإن كنت لا تؤمن بهذا فتصحيح أصل الإيمان بالملائكة والوحي أهم عليك، وإن كنت آمنت به وجوزت أنه يشاهد النبي مالا تشاهده الأمة فكيف لا تجوز هذا في الميت؟
It is not difficult for Allah, exalted be His majesty, to revert life again to the atoms of the body, whether they are gathered in a grave, or scattered in a desert, or dispersed in the belly of a beast, with that question and answer, and he sees the angel who questions him and speaks to him. And there is no hope in knowing how that is analytically, for the realities of the afterlife are related to another system completely different from the system of this visible world of the living. And we will quote for you in explaining this issue what Imam al-Ghazali (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'This eye is not fit to observe the malakut (angelic realm) matters, and everything related to the Hereafter is from the world of malakut. Do you not see the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) how they used to believe in the descent of Jibril, and they did not see him, and they believed that he (peace be upon him) sees him? If you do not believe in this, then correcting the foundation of belief in angels and revelation is more important for you. And if you believe in it and accept that he sees what the nation does not see, then why do you not accept this regarding the deceased?'
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage argues for the reality of resurrection and the questioning in the grave from an epistemological perspective. The author first states that it is easy for Allah to restore life to atoms regardless of their location, and that the deceased perceives the angel of death and answers questions. He then emphasizes that the exact nature of these events cannot be known through analysis because the afterlife follows a completely different order from the visible world. To clarify, he quotes Imam al-Ghazali: the physical eye is incapable of perceiving the malakut (angelic realm); every afterlife matter belongs to that realm. Al-Ghazali draws an analogy with the Companions: they believed in Jibril's descent without seeing him, and they believed that the Prophet saw him. If one cannot accept that the deceased sees what the living cannot, then the very foundation of belief in angels and revelation is at stake. Thus, the argument is that belief in unseen realities, including the grave's events, is required by the same principle that underlies belief in revelation.

Key Terms
السؤال والجواب
الملكوت
جبريل
العين لا تصلح
نظام آخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The events of the grave (questioning, seeing angels) can be scientifically analyzed or empirically verified.
Correction: The passage clarifies that these events belong to a completely different system (malakut) that is beyond sensory perception; they must be accepted through revelation, not analysis.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali's quote, why should we accept that the deceased sees the angel even though we cannot see it?
A) Because it is physically proven.
B) Because the Companions saw the Prophet seeing Jibril, and the same principle applies to the deceased.
C) Because everyone sees it in the grave.
D) Because the eye can be trained to see angels.

Key Takeaway
The events of the grave and resurrection are unseen realities that must be accepted by the same principle of faith that accepts angels and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you honestly say that your belief in the events of the grave is as firm as your belief in angels? If not, what does that reveal about your reliance on sensory evidence over revelation? Today, commit to strengthening your iman in all unseen matters by reflecting on the principle al-Ghazali lays out.
?
When you think about your own grave and the questioning that awaits, do you find yourself demanding proof or comfort from the physical world? How does the lesson's reminder that the afterlife belongs to a different system challenge you to trust Allah's word alone? What practical step can you take to make that trust more real?
?
The Companions believed that the Prophet saw Jibril without seeing him themselves. Do you accept that same principle for the deceased? If there is any hesitation, what is its root? Pray to Allah to remove that hesitation and to grant you true, unshakeable faith in the unseen.

Four Textual Proofs for the Reality of Punishment and Bliss in the Grave
Al-Buti presents four textual proofs for the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four scriptural proofs from the Quran and Sunna that establish the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave, and how each proof demonstrates this intermediate state between death and resurrection.

Core Idea
The punishment and bliss of the grave are established by certain, mutawatir reports from the Quran and Sunna.

In this lesson, we examine four pieces of textual evidence that Shaykh al-Buti presents as decisive proofs for the reality of grave punishment and bliss. These proofs are drawn from the Quran and authentic hadiths, and they collectively establish this unseen reality as a matter of certain belief (yaqini). The author emphasizes that since these are matters outside sensory perception and rational deduction, we rely on transmitted reports (samiyyat). Let's explore each proof and understand how it supports the doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the structured presentation: an introductory statement followed by four numbered proofs. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you analyze.
The passage is from al-Buti's work on certain beliefs.
2
Understand the first two Quranic verses
Identify the verses from Surah al-An'am and Surah Muhammad. Note that they describe punishment at the moment of death. The author clarifies that although the punishment occurs before burial, it is attributed to the grave because most of it occurs there.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.
3
Analyze the second Quranic verse
Examine the verse from Surah Ghafir. The key point is the conjunction of 'morning and evening' with 'the Day of Resurrection', indicating a punishment before the final judgment—thus in the grave.
The author references al-Mawaqif for further detail.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
Study the hadith about the two graves (from Ibn Abbas) and the hadith about the deceased being shown his seat (from Ibn Umar). Both directly describe punishment or bliss occurring after death and before resurrection.
These hadiths are mutawatir in meaning.
5
Synthesize the cumulative evidence
Reflect on how all four proofs together establish the doctrine as a matter of certain belief. Notice that the author relies solely on transmitted reports, not reason or observation.
This demonstrates the samiyyat methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج - عذاب القبر ونعيمه: وهما من الحقائق الغيبية التي ثبت الدليل عليها أيضاً بالخبر اليقيني المتواتر. ولنذكر لك طائفة من هذه الأخبار، إذ هي العمدة في موقفنا من المغيبات التي لا مجال للمشاهدة والعقل في الخوض فيها.
1 - يقول الله تعالى: ( ولو ترى إذ الظالمون في غمرات الموت والملائكة باسطوا أيديهم أخرجوا أنفسكم، اليوم تجزون عذاب الهون ) [الأنعام: 93]. ومثله قوله تعالى: ( فكيف إذا توفتهم الملائكة يضربون وجوههم وأدبارهم ) [محمد: 27]. ولا يخدش في دلالة الآيتين على ما نقول، أن العذاب كائن - في دلالتها - من قبل الدفن، إذ هو على كل من جملة العذاب الواقع قبل يوم القيامة، ونحن إنما نضيف العذاب إلى القبر لأنه معظمه يقع فيه، كما أوضحنا أنفاً (1) (انظر فتح الباري: 3-151).
2 - يقول الله تعالى: ( وحاق بآل فرعون سوء العذاب، النار يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً ويوم تقوم الساعة أدخلوا آل فرعون أشد العذاب ) [غافر: 45-46]. ووجه دلالة الآية أنه لما عطف فيها قوله: ويوم تقوم على: غدواً وعشياً، علمنا يقيناً أن النار التي يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً غير التي يعرضون عليها يوم القيامة، ولا شك أنه واقع ما بين الموت والنشور (2) (انظر المواقف وشرحه للايجي: 42-52).
3 - روى البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مر على قبرين فقال: « إنهما ليعذبان، وما يعذبان في كبير » ثم قال: « أما أحدهما فكان يسعى بالنميمة، وأما الآخر فكان لا يستتر من بوله » ثم أخذ عوداً رطباً فكسره باثنتين، ثم غرز كل واحد منهما على قبر، ثم قال: « لعله يخفف عنها مالم ييبسا » (3) (هكذا في أكثر الروايات بلفظ « يستتر » أي لا يجعل بينه وبين بوله سترة، فهو لا يتحفظ منه، ورواية مسلم وأبي داود « يستنزه ». وفي رواية لابن عساكر « يستبرئ » والمعنى في كلها واحد أو متقارب).
4 - روى البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما عن نافع عن ابن عمر أن رسول الله قال: « إن أحدكم إذا مات عرض عليه مقعده بالغداة والعشي إن كان من أهل الجنة فمن أهل الجنة، وإن كان من أهل النار فمن أهل النار، يقال له: هذا مقعدك حتى يبعثك الله يوم القيامة ». ولاشك أن في هذا تنعيماً لمن هو من أهل الجنة وتعذيباً لمن هو من أهل النار.
C - Punishment and bliss of the grave: Both of them are from the unseen realities which have also been established by the certain, mutawatir report. And we will mention for you a group of these reports, for they are the mainstay in our stance regarding the unseen matters which have no room for observation or reason to delve into. 
1 - Allah Almighty says: 'And if you could see when the wrongdoers are in the agonies of death and the angels are stretching out their hands, [saying], "Give up your souls. Today you will be recompensed with the punishment of humiliation..."' [Al-An'am: 93]. And similar is His statement: 'Then how will it be when the angels take them at death, striking their faces and their backs?' [Muhammad: 27]. And there is no harm to the indication of the two verses concerning what we say, that the punishment occurs – in their indication – before burial, for it is absolutely part of the punishment that occurs before the Day of Resurrection. And we only attribute the punishment to the grave because most of it occurs therein, as we have explained earlier (1) (See Fath al-Bari: 3-151).
2 - Allah Almighty says: 'And the worst punishment encompassed the people of Pharaoh. The Fire is shown to them morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour is established [it will be said], "Admit the people of Pharaoh into the severest punishment."' [Ghafir: 45-46]. And the aspect of the verse's indication is that when His statement 'and on the Day the Hour is established' is conjoined to 'morning and evening', we know with certainty that the Fire which is shown to them morning and evening is other than the one to which they will be exposed on the Day of Resurrection, and there is no doubt that it occurs between death and resurrection (2) (See al-Mawaqif and its commentary by al-Iji: 42-52).
3 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) passed by two graves and said: 'Indeed, they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something great.' Then he said: 'As for one of them, he used to go about with slander, and as for the other, he used not to take precautions from his urine.' Then he took a fresh palm branch and split it into two, then planted each one on a grave, then said: 'Perhaps it will be lightened for them as long as they do not dry out.' (3) (This is in most narrations with the word 'yastatiru', i.e., he does not put a barrier between himself and his urine, so he does not guard himself. Muslim and Abu Dawud have 'yastanziho' (abstains). In a narration from Ibn Asakir, 'yastabri'u' (cleans himself). The meaning in all is one or close.)
4 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others narrated from Nafi' from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you dies, his seat is shown to him morning and evening. If he is from the people of Paradise, then he is from the people of Paradise; and if he is from the people of Hellfire, then he is from the people of Hellfire. It is said to him: This is your seat until Allah raises you on the Day of Resurrection.' And there is no doubt that in this is bliss for those who are from the people of Paradise and punishment for those who are from the people of Hellfire.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is an evidentiary compilation where the author asserts that punishment and bliss of the grave are established by certain transmitted evidence (al-khabar al-yaqini al-mutawatir). He then presents four pieces of evidence in sequence. 

First evidence: Two Quranic verses – the first shows the angels taking souls with punishment, the second shows them striking faces and backs at death. The author clarifies that although the verses describe punishment before burial, it is called 'punishment of the grave' because most of it occurs there. A footnote references Fath al-Bari. 

Second evidence: The verse from Surah Ghafir shows the people of Pharaoh being exposed to the Fire morning and evening. The author argues that since 'morning and evening' is contrasted with 'the Day the Hour is established', this exposure must occur between death and resurrection—hence, this is the punishment of the grave. The footnote references al-Mawaqif. 

Third evidence: A hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet passes by two graves being punished for petty sins: slander and not cleaning after urination. The Prophet plants a fresh branch, hoping it will lighten their punishment until it dries. The footnote clarifies the wording 'yastatiru' and variants. 

Fourth evidence: A hadith from Ibn Umar stating that the deceased is shown his seat in Paradise or Hell morning and evening. The author concludes this clearly indicates either bliss or punishment. 

Each piece is presented as a cumulative proof for the doctrine of grave punishment and bliss, relying entirely on scriptural and prophetic authority (samiyyat).

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
نعيم القبر
خبر يقيني متواتر
غمرات الموت
عرض على النار
مقعده بالغداة والعشي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the 'punishment of the grave' refers only to torment after burial, excluding events at death.
Correction: The author clarifies that the punishment includes events at death and before resurrection, but is attributed to the grave because most of it occurs there.

Checkpoint
How does the verse about Pharaoh's people in Surah Ghafir serve as evidence for punishment in the grave?
A) It mentions fire that occurs after resurrection.
B) It shows fire in the grave itself.
C) The conjunction of 'morning and evening' with 'the Day of Resurrection' indicates a punishment before the final judgment.
D) It describes the destruction of Pharaoh's army.

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the grave are established by certain, mutawatir reports from the Quran and Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your seat in Paradise or Hell were shown to you every morning and evening after you die starting tonight, what would you see? Does that thought change how you will act in the next hour?
?
The Prophet said the punishment of two people was lightened by a fresh branch because it glorifies Allah. Is there any believing dead person in your life whose punishment you hope is being lightened? What are you doing, right now, to increase the chances that they receive mercy?
?
You have just read four certain proofs that the grave holds either bliss or torment. If you were to die tonight, would the punishment or bliss begin immediately? What habit do you need to break or start today to ensure your seat is shown in Paradise?

Scriptural Evidence for the Punishment of the Grave
Buti enumerates three scriptural proofs for punishment and bliss of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Quranic and hadith proofs that establish the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave.

Core Idea
The grave's reward and punishment are proven by decisive texts from the Quran and Sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the primary scriptural evidence that the punishment and bliss of the grave are real. Imam al-Buti presents a Quranic verse and two authentic hadiths that together form a strong foundation for this doctrine, demonstrating that it is not a matter of mere speculation but of divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Surah Ghafir (40:45-46) carefully. The key is the coordination of 'morning and evening' with 'the Day the Hour establishes', which shows two different times of exposure to the Fire.
The phrase 'morning and evening' indicates a regular occurrence before the Resurrection.
2
Examine the first hadith
Read the hadith about the Prophet passing by two graves and the explanation of their punishment. Note that the punishment is happening in the grave itself, and the fresh branch symbolizes alleviation.
This hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, the most authentic collections.
3
Examine the second hadith
Read the hadith about the deceased being shown his seat morning and evening. This implies ongoing reward or punishment from the moment of death until the Resurrection.
The phrase 'morning and evening' mirrors the Quranic verse.
4
Reflect on collective strength
After reading all three proofs, consider how they complement each other and strengthen the overall case for the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave.
Multiple sources from different Companions and contexts increase certainty.

And the aspect of indication of the verse is that when His statement 'and on the Day the Hour establishes' is coordinated with 'morning and evening', we know with certainty that the Fire to which they are exposed morning and evening is other than that to which they are exposed on the Day of Resurrection, and there is no doubt that it occurs between death and resurrection.
3 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim and others narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, passed by two graves and said: 'Indeed they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something major.' Then he said: 'As for one of them, he used to spread slander, and as for the other, he did not protect himself from his urine.' Then he took a fresh branch, broke it in two, then planted each piece on a grave, then said: 'Perhaps it will be lightened for them as long as they do not dry out.'
4 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim and others narrated from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you dies, his seat is shown to him morning and evening. If he is from the people of Paradise, then from the people of Paradise, and if he is from the people of Hellfire, then from the people of Hellfire. It is said to him: This is your seat until Allah resurrects you on the Day of Resurrection.' There is no doubt that in this is bliss for those who are from the people of Paradise and punishment for those who are from the people of Hellfire.
(1) See Fath al-Bari: 3/151 (2) See al-Mawaqif with its commentary by al-Iji: 42-52 (3) This is in most narrations with the wording 'yastatir', i.e., he does not place a barrier between himself and his urine, so he does not guard against it; Muslim and Abu Dawud have 'yastanzih'; and in a narration of Ibn 'Asakir 'yastabri''; the meaning in all is one or close.
So these are some of the texts in the Book and the Sunnah about the punishment and bliss of the grave, and collectively they exceed the threshold of tawatur required for certainty of indication upon the content, and therefore the consensus of Muslims occurred that the deceased is exposed before the resurrection to punishment or bliss in his state, just as their consensus occurred on the seizure of the soul by the Angel of Death and on the questioning by the two angels after death.
If you know this, we say:
As for denying the punishment of the grave entirely, it is a slide into disbelief, because of the decisive evidence established concerning it as you know.
As for acknowledging it in principle, while having doubt about whether it is for the soul only, or for the soul together with the body or some parts of the body, that is a matter that does not lead the researcher – whichever direction he takes – to disbelief, because the investigation into whether the punishment is for the soul only or for the soul and body together is subject to examination, and there are no clear decisive proofs in it like the proofs for the principle of punishment and bliss.
However, Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah and the majority of Muslims said that it is for the soul and body together, because it is from the category of the possible, as we explained above, and because the apparent meaning of the texts requires that and there is no need for reinterpretation. For it is established in the Sahih that the Messenger stood over the well into which the bodies of the polytheists were thrown on the day of Badr, and he began speaking to them, saying: 'We have indeed found what our Lord promised us to be true; have you found what your Lord promised you to be true?' And were it not for his knowledge that the bodies themselves are what hear his speech, he would not have directed his address to them, and he would not have said to 'Umar when he wondered at his addressing those bodies: 'By Him in whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, you are not more hearers of what I say than they.'
(1) See what we mentioned about the barzakh life of the dead in the explanation of this hadith in the book (Fiqh al-Sirah).
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and ruling structure. The author first presents four pieces of evidence for the punishment and bliss of the grave: two from the Quran (the first is a general statement about punishment before resurrection; the second is the verse about Pharaoh's people being exposed to the Fire morning and evening) and two from hadith (the Prophet's encounter with the two punished graves and the hadith about the deceased being shown his seat morning and evening). He then concludes that the collective evidence reaches the level of tawatur (mass transmission), yielding certainty, and that Muslim consensus confirms it.

Next, he distinguishes two doctrines: (1) denying the punishment entirely—this leads to kufr (disbelief) because the evidence is decisive; (2) accepting the principle but speculating whether the punishment affects only the soul or the soul and body together—this does not lead to kufr because the modality lacks equally decisive proof and is open to investigation.

Finally, he states the position of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: the punishment affects both soul and body together, based on logical possibility (it is not impossible) and the apparent meaning of texts, citing the hadith of the Prophet addressing the dead polytheists at Badr, which implies the bodies (or the graves) hear, hence the punishment involves the body as well. The author uses this hadith to argue that the bodies themselves are addressed, so they must be capable of perception, supporting the view that punishment and bliss affect both soul and body in the barzakh.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
غدو
عشي
نميمة

According to the hadith from Ibn 'Abbas, what were the reasons for the punishment of the two people in the graves?
A) Murder and theft
B) Slander and not protecting oneself from urine
C) Hypocrisy and lying
D) Disobeying parents and drinking alcohol

Key Takeaway
The Quran and authentic hadiths provide clear evidence that punishment and bliss begin in the grave before the Resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were shown your seat in the grave right now—morning and evening—would you be comforted or terrified? What does that reveal about your current state of faith and deeds?
?
In the hadith, the Prophet mentioned two specific sins that led to punishment: spreading slander and not protecting from urine. Which of these do you take lightly? What concrete step will you take today to guard against that sin?
?
The Prophet interceded for the two deceased by planting a branch to lighten their punishment. Do you crave the Prophet's intercession? What have you done—or failed to do—that makes you deserving of it?

Consensus and Certainty of the Grave's Punishment
Buti asserts the tawatur and consensus of the grave's punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the collective evidence for the punishment of the grave reaches the level of tawatur and why it is a matter of consensus.

Core Idea
The evidence for punishment in the grave is mass-transmitted and agreed upon by Muslims.

After presenting the scriptural proofs, Imam al-Buti explains that these texts collectively surpass the threshold of tawatur (mass transmission), rendering the doctrine of punishment and bliss in the grave certain. Furthermore, the entire Muslim community has reached consensus on this issue, just as they have on other matters of the unseen. This lesson explores that conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tawatur
Read the sentence where the author states that the texts 'exceed the threshold of tawatur required for certainty of indication upon the content.' Understand that tawatur means multiple independent chains of transmission that preclude the possibility of collusion.
Tawatur is a key concept in Islamic epistemology; it yields certain knowledge.
2
Note the consensus
The author then mentions that the consensus (ijma') of Muslims has occurred on this matter, just as on other matters like the questioning by the two angels.
Consensus is another source of certainty in Islamic theology.
3
Reflect on the link
Connect the tawatur of the texts to the consensus. The abundance of authentic texts leads to consensus, and together they make the doctrine undeniable.
This is similar to the methodology used for other essential beliefs.

دلالتها - من قبل الدفن ، إذ هو على كل من جملة العذاب الواقع قبل يوم القيامة ، ونحن إنما نضيف العذاب إلى القبر لأنه معظمه يقع فيه ، كما أوضحنــا أنفا . الساعة
٢ - يقول الله تعالى : ﴿ وَحاق بِآلِ فِرْعَوْنَ سُوءُ الْعَذَابِ ، النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوًّا وَعَشِيًّا وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا آلَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ [ غافر : ٤٥ - ٤٦ ] . ووجه دلالة الآية أنه لما عُطف فيها قوله : ويوم تقوم على : غدواً وعشياً ، علمنا يقيناً أن النار التي يعرضون عليها غدواً وعشياً غير التي يعرضون عليها يوم القيامة ، ولا شك أنه واقع ما بين الموت والنشور .
٣ - روى البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مر على قبرين فقال : « إنها ليعذبان ، وما يعذبان في كبير » ثم قال : « أما أحدهما فكان يسعى بالنميمة ، وأما الآخر فكان لا يستتر من بوله » . ثم أخذ عوداً رطباً فكسره باثنتين ، ثم غرز كل واحد منهما على قبر ، ثم قال : « لعلـه يخفف عنها مالم ييبسا » .
٤ - روى البخاري ومسلم وغيرهما عن نافع عن ابن عمر أن رسول الله قال : « إن أحدكم إذا مات عُرض عليه مقعده بالغداة والعشي إن كان من أهل الجنة فمن أهل الجنة ، وإن كان من أهل النار فمن أهل النار ، يقال له : هذا مقعدك حتى يبعثك الله يوم القيامة » . ولاشك أن في هذا تنعيماً لمن هو من أهل الجنة وتعذيباً لمن هو من أهل النار .
(۱) انظر فتح الباري : ٣ - ١٥١ (۲) انظر المواقف وشرحه للايجي : ٤٢ - ٥٢ (۳) هكذا في أكثر الروايات بلفظ « يستتر » أي لا يجعل بينه وبين بوله سترة ، فهو لا يتحفظ منه ، ورواية مسلم وأبي داود » يستنزه » . وفي رواية لابن عساكر « يستبرئ » والمعنى في كلها واحد أو متقارب .
فهذه بعض النصوص الواردة في الكتاب والسنة عن عذاب القبر ونعيمه وهي في مجموعها تتجاوز حد التواتر المطلوب لقطعية الدلالة على المضمون ولذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على أن الميت يتعرض قبل النشور للعذاب أو للنعيم حاله كما تم إجماعهم على قبض ملك الموت للروح وعلى سؤال الملكين من حال بعد الموت .
إذا علمت هذا فإننا نقول :

(۱) انظر ماذكرناه عن الحياة البرزخية للأموات عند شرح هذا الحديث في كتاب ( فقه السيرة ) .

Ruling on Denial and Modality of Punishment
Buti rules on denial and discusses the nature of punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on denying the punishment of the grave and the difference between rejecting the principle and speculating about its modality.

Core Idea
Denying the punishment of the grave leads to disbelief, but speculating on how it affects soul and body does not.

Imam al-Buti now turns to the implications of the established doctrine. He makes a critical distinction: outright denial of the punishment of the grave is a slide into disbelief (kufr) because the evidence is decisive. However, if one accepts the principle but has doubt about whether the punishment affects only the soul or both soul and body, that does not lead to kufr, as the modality is not proven by equally decisive evidence. He then presents the majority Sunni position that the punishment affects both soul and body.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the section beginning 'If you know this, we say:'. The author presents two distinct situations: denial of the principle, and doubt about the modality.
Note the use of 'أما' and 'وأما' to contrast the two.
2
Understand why denial is kufr
The author says denial is a 'slide into disbelief' because of the decisive evidence. Reflect on the strength of the proofs from the previous lesson.
This shows that beliefs established by certain evidence are non-negotiable.
3
Understand why doubt on modality is not kufr
The author explains that the modality (soul alone or soul and body) is subject to investigation and lacks clear decisive proofs. So differing or doubting does not lead to disbelief.
This tolerance allows for scholarly discussion on secondary aspects.
4
Learn the Sunni position
Read the final part where the author states the view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: punishment affects both soul and body together, supported by logical possibility and apparent meaning of texts, especially the hadith of addressing the dead at Badr.
This is the mainstream view, but not absolutely binding on every Muslim.

أما إنكار عذاب القبر ، من أصله ، فهو مزلق إلى الكفر ، لما ثبت من الدليل القاطع فيه كما علمت .
وإما إقراره من حيث الأصل ، مع الارتياب في أنه يكون للروح فقط ، أو للروح مع الجسم أو بعض أجزاء الجسم ، فذلك أمر ليس من شأنه أن ينتهي بالباحث - إلى أي الاتجاهين ذهب - إلى الكفر لأن التحقيق في أن العذاب يكون للروح فقط أو للروح والجسد معاً ، خاضع للنظر ، وليست فيه أدلة قاطعة واضحة كأدلة أصل التعذيب والتنعيم .
غير أن أهل السنة والجماعة وجمهور المسلمين ، قالوا بأن ذلك يكون للروح والجسد معاً ، إذ هو من قبيل الممكن ، كما أوضحنا أنفاً ، ولأن ظاهر النصوص الواردة تقتضي ذلك ولا حاجة إلى التأويل . فقد ثبت في الصحيح أن الرسول وقف على القليب الذي ألقيت فيه جثث المشركين يوم بدر ، وأخذ يكلمهم قائلاً : « إنا قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقاً ، فهل وجدتم ما وعد ربكم حقاً » . ولولا علمه أن الأجداث بنفسها هي التي تسمع كلامه ، لما اتجه في خطابه إليها ، ولما قال لعمر لما تعجب من مخاطبته لتلك الأجساد : « والذي نفس محمد بيده ما أنتم بأسمع لما أقول منهم » .
(۱) انظر ماذكرناه عن الحياة البرزخية للأموات عند شرح هذا الحديث في كتاب ( فقه السيرة ) .
Its indication - before burial, since it is part of the punishment occurring before the Day of Resurrection, and we only attribute the punishment to the grave because most of it occurs in it, as we explained above. The Hour.
2 - Allah Almighty says: {And the evil punishment encompassed the people of Pharaoh; the Fire they are exposed to morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour establishes: 'Admit the people of Pharaoh into the severest punishment'} [Ghafir: 45-46]. And the aspect of indication of the verse is that when His statement 'and on the Day the Hour establishes' is coordinated with 'morning and evening', we know with certainty that the Fire to which they are exposed morning and evening is other than that to which they are exposed on the Day of Resurrection, and there is no doubt that it occurs between death and resurrection.
3 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim and others narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, passed by two graves and said: 'Indeed they are being punished, and they are not being punished for something major.' Then he said: 'As for one of them, he used to spread slander, and as for the other, he did not protect himself from his urine.' Then he took a fresh branch, broke it in two, then planted each piece on a grave, then said: 'Perhaps it will be lightened for them as long as they do not dry out.'
4 - Al-Bukhari, Muslim and others narrated from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you dies, his seat is shown to him morning and evening. If he is from the people of Paradise, then from the people of Paradise, and if he is from the people of Hellfire, then from the people of Hellfire. It is said to him: This is your seat until Allah resurrects you on the Day of Resurrection.' There is no doubt that in this is bliss for those who are from the people of Paradise and punishment for those who are from the people of Hellfire.
(1) See Fath al-Bari: 3/151 (2) See al-Mawaqif with its commentary by al-Iji: 42-52 (3) This is in most narrations with the wording 'yastatir', i.e., he does not place a barrier between himself and his urine, so he does not guard against it; Muslim and Abu Dawud have 'yastanzih'; and in a narration of Ibn 'Asakir 'yastabri''; the meaning in all is one or close.
So these are some of the texts in the Book and the Sunnah about the punishment and bliss of the grave, and collectively they exceed the threshold of tawatur required for certainty of indication upon the content, and therefore the consensus of Muslims occurred that the deceased is exposed before the resurrection to punishment or bliss in his state, just as their consensus occurred on the seizure of the soul by the Angel of Death and on the questioning by the two angels after death.
If you know this, we say:
As for denying the punishment of the grave entirely, it is a slide into disbelief, because of the decisive evidence established concerning it as you know.
As for acknowledging it in principle, while having doubt about whether it is for the soul only, or for the soul together with the body or some parts of the body, that is a matter that does not lead the researcher – whichever direction he takes – to disbelief, because the investigation into whether the punishment is for the soul only or for the soul and body together is subject to examination, and there are no clear decisive proofs in it like the proofs for the principle of punishment and bliss.
However, Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah and the majority of Muslims said that it is for the soul and body together, because it is from the category of the possible, as we explained above, and because the apparent meaning of the texts requires that and there is no need for reinterpretation. For it is established in the Sahih that the Messenger stood over the well into which the bodies of the polytheists were thrown on the day of Badr, and he began speaking to them, saying: 'We have indeed found what our Lord promised us to be true; have you found what your Lord promised you to be true?' And were it not for his knowledge that the bodies themselves are what hear his speech, he would not have directed his address to them, and he would not have said to 'Umar when he wondered at his addressing those bodies: 'By Him in whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, you are not more hearers of what I say than they.'
(1) See what we mentioned about the barzakh life of the dead in the explanation of this hadith in the book (Fiqh al-Sirah).
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and ruling structure. The author first presents four pieces of evidence for the punishment and bliss of the grave: two from the Quran (the first is a general statement about punishment before resurrection; the second is the verse about Pharaoh's people being exposed to the Fire morning and evening) and two from hadith (the Prophet's encounter with the two punished graves and the hadith about the deceased being shown his seat morning and evening). He then concludes that the collective evidence reaches the level of tawatur (mass transmission), yielding certainty, and that Muslim consensus confirms it.

Next, he distinguishes two doctrines: (1) denying the punishment entirely—this leads to kufr (disbelief) because the evidence is decisive; (2) accepting the principle but speculating whether the punishment affects only the soul or the soul and body together—this does not lead to kufr because the modality lacks equally decisive proof and is open to investigation.

Finally, he states the position of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: the punishment affects both soul and body together, based on logical possibility (it is not impossible) and the apparent meaning of texts, citing the hadith of the Prophet addressing the dead polytheists at Badr, which implies the bodies (or the graves) hear, hence the punishment involves the body as well. The author uses this hadith to argue that the bodies themselves are addressed, so they must be capable of perception, supporting the view that punishment and bliss affect both soul and body in the barzakh.

Key Terms
كفر
روح
جسد
دليل قاطع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any doubt or disagreement about the nature of punishment in the grave leads to disbelief.
Correction: Buti clarifies that denying the principle is kufr, but doubting or differing on the modality (soul alone vs. soul and body) is not kufr, as the evidence for the modality is not decisive.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the ruling on someone who acknowledges the punishment of the grave but doubts whether it affects the soul alone or the soul and body together?
A) Such doubt leads to disbelief because it contradicts the consensus.
B) It does not lead to disbelief because the modality is not proven by decisive evidence.
C) It leads to disbelief only if the person also denies the resurrection.
D) It is permissible but sinful.

Key Takeaway
Denying the punishment of the grave is disbelief, but speculating on its modality is not; the Sunni view is that it affects soul and body together.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may acknowledge the punishment of the grave in theory, but have you ever secretly doubted whether it applies to you? How does the Prophet's speech to the dead at Badr challenge your assumptions about the reality of the grave?
?
Do you truly believe that your body will experience punishment or bliss in the grave? If so, how should that affect how you treat your body today? What concrete changes will you make?
?
The author distinguishes between decisive evidence and less certain matters. In your own faith, are you careful to distinguish between core beliefs and secondary details? Where might you be conflating them, and how will you adjust your thinking?

The Decisive Proof for Grave Punishment
Buti establishes tawatur and ijma' on grave punishment and issues ruling on denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the texts on grave punishment are considered decisive and what the ruling is on denying them.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is established by mass-transmitted texts, making denial a dangerous deviation.

Buti opens by presenting the cumulative evidence for grave punishment and bliss. He emphasizes that these texts collectively reach the level of tawatur, which gives certainty. Consequently, the Muslim consensus has affirmed the reality of this intermediate state. This passage then draws a sharp line: outright denial of grave punishment is a path to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Buti uses a very compact style here, moving from evidence to ruling.
2
Identify the two bases: tawatur and ijma'
Find where Buti mentions that the texts exceed the limit of tawatur and that Muslims have consensus on grave punishment and bliss.
Tawatur means mass transmission that yields certainty; ijma' is consensus.
3
Understand the ruling on denial
Buti states that denying grave punishment 'from its origin' is a slippery slope to kufr. Reflect on what 'from its origin' means — complete rejection.
This does not apply to those who affirm the principle but differ on details.
4
Connect to the broader topic of samiyyat
This passage belongs to the category of samiyyat (matters of the unseen). Note that belief in grave punishment is part of Islamic creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذه بعض النصوص الواردة في الكتاب والسنة عن عذاب القبر ونعيمه وهي في مجموعها تتجاوز حد التواتر المطلوب لقطعية الدلالة على المضمون ولذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على أن الميت يتعرض قبل النشور للعذاب أو للنعيم حاله كما تم إجماعهم على قبض ملك الموت للروح وعلى سؤال الملكين من بعد الموت . إذا علمت هذا فإننا نقول : أما إنكار عذاب القبر ، من أصله ، فهو مزلق إلى الكفر ، لما ثبت من الدليل القاطع فيه كما علمت .
These are some texts in the Book and the Sunnah about the punishment and bliss of the grave, and they collectively exceed the limit of tawatur required for definitive indication of the content. Therefore, the Muslims have consensus that the deceased, before the resurrection, is exposed to punishment or bliss in his state, just as they have consensus on the Angel of Death's taking of the soul and on the questioning of the two angels after death. If you know this, we say: As for denying the punishment of the grave, from its origin, it is a slippery slope to disbelief, because of the decisive proof established in it as you have known.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage establishes the definitive nature of the texts on grave punishment and bliss, and states the ruling on denial. Buti begins by noting that the combined texts from the Quran and Sunnah on this topic reach the level of tawatur (mass transmission), which yields certainty. Because of this, the Muslim community has reached consensus (ijma') on two facts: (1) that the deceased before the resurrection experiences either punishment or bliss in the grave, and (2) that the Angel of Death takes the soul and the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) question the deceased after burial. Then Buti delivers a ruling: to deny the reality of grave punishment from its very basis leads to kufr (disbelief), because it contradicts a matter established by decisive proof. This is a stern warning, but it is limited to outright denial, not to speculation about its modality.

إجماع

كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that texts on grave punishment are not decisive and that denial is a matter of interpretation.
Correction: Buti argues that the texts are mutawatir and thus yield certainty; he also states that denying them from the root leads to kufr.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the ruling on someone who denies the punishment of the grave from its origin?
A) It is a minor sin
B) It is a slippery slope to kufr (disbelief)
C) It is permissible if they interpret metaphorically
D) It is a matter of ijtihad

Key Takeaway
Grave punishment is established by decisive proofs; denying it outright is a form of disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in the punishment of the grave with the same certainty you believe in the five daily prayers? If your belief is weaker, what does that reveal about your heart's connection to the unseen? Take a moment tonight to recite the Prophet's du'a for protection from the grave's punishment and mean it.
?
If the Prophet (peace be upon him) warned so strongly about grave punishment, why do you not feel fear when you sin? Is it because you have not internalized this decisive proof? What sin are you committing right now that you would not dare commit if you expected to be questioned by Munkar and Nakir within hours?
?
The lesson says denial of grave punishment is a slippery slope to disbelief. Have you ever doubted its reality or felt it is unimportant? If so, what concrete step will you take this week to strengthen your conviction—such as studying the proofs more deeply or sharing the teaching with a friend?

Grave Punishment: For Soul and Body Together
Buti affirms Sunni view that grave punishment affects soul and body together.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that grave punishment affects both soul and body, along with the evidence and reasoning supporting it.

Core Idea
Grave punishment involves both soul and body, as the apparent meaning of texts shows.

This lesson explores a secondary issue within the belief in grave punishment: is it only for the soul or for both soul and body? Buti clarifies that while the original fact is proven by decisive evidence, the modality is open to ijtihad, yet the Sunni consensus is clear. Let's examine the arguments and the prophetic proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the issue and its stakes
Recognize that differing on this specific question does not lead to disbelief, but the Sunni view is based on textual evidence.
Buti emphasizes that the original reality of grave punishment is established by decisive proofs.
2
Examine the Sunni position and its two reasons
The majority say punishment is for soul and body together. Buti gives two reasons: rational possibility and the apparent meaning of texts without ta'wil.
The second reason is supported by the hadith of the Prophet addressing the dead at Badr.
3
Consider the minority view and logical conclusion
A minority holds it is only for the soul. The majority responds that they have no proof for specification. If one accepts original reality, they can accept the majority view without evidence to the contrary.
Buti's logical argument: without proof for ta'wil, the apparent meaning stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إقراره من حيث الأصل ، مع الارتياب في أنه يكون للروح فقط ، أو للروح مع الجسم أو بعض أجزاء الجسم ، فذلك أمر ليس من شأنه أن ينتهي بالباحث - إلى أي الاتجاهين ذهب - إلى الكفر لأن التحقيق في أن العذاب يكون للروح فقط أو للروح والجسد معاً ، خاضع للنظر ، وليست فيه أدلة قاطعة واضحة كأدلة أصل التعذيب والتنعيم . غير أن أهل السنة والجماعة وجمهور المسلمين ، قالوا بأن ذلك يكون للروح والجسد معاً ، إذ هو من قبيل الممكن ، كما أوضحنا أنفاً ، ولأن ظاهر النصوص الواردة تقتضي ذلك ولا حاجة إلى التأويل . فقد ثبت في الصحيح أن الرسول وقف على القليب الذي ألقيت فيه جثث المشركين يوم بدر ، وأخذ يكلمهم قائلاً : « إنا قد وجدنا ما وعدنا ربنا حقاً ، فهل وجدتم ما وعد ربكم حقاً » . ولولا علمه أن الأجداث بنفسها هي التي تسمع كلامه ، لما اتجه في خطابه إليها ، ولما قال لعمر لما تعجب من مخاطبته لتلك الأجساد : « والذي نفس محمد بيده ما أنتم بأسمع لما أقول منهم » . وذهبت طائفة قليلة أخرى إلى أن ذلك كله إنما يكون للروح فقط ، قال الجمهور : وليس لهم من دليل على التخصيص والتأويل . والذي يؤمن بأصل العذاب والنعيم في القبر للروح ، يستطيع أن يؤمن بها للروح مع الجسد ، وإذا لم يرد دليل على التأويل والتخصيص فإن القول بهما قول بما لا دليل عليه
As for affirming it in principle, while being doubtful whether it is for the soul only or for the soul together with the body or some parts of the body, that is a matter that will not lead the researcher - whichever direction he takes - to disbelief, because the verification of whether the punishment is for the soul only or for the soul and body together is subject to examination, and there are no clear decisive proofs in it like the proofs for the origin of punishment and bliss. However, Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah and the majority of Muslims said that it is for the soul and body together, since it is among possibilities, as we have explained earlier, and because the apparent meaning of the texts that have come requires that and there is no need for interpretation (ta'wil). It is established in the authentic hadith that the Messenger stood at the well where the bodies of the polytheists on the day of Badr were thrown, and he began addressing them, saying: 'Indeed, we have found what our Lord promised us to be true; have you found what your Lord promised you to be true?' And if he did not know that the bodies themselves were the ones that hear his speech, he would not have directed his address to them, and he would not have said to 'Umar when 'Umar was astonished at his addressing those bodies: 'By Him in Whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, you are not more attentive to what I say than they are.' And another small group held that all of that is only for the soul. The majority said: They have no proof for specification and interpretation. And whoever believes in the origin of punishment and bliss in the grave for the soul, he can believe in it for the soul together with the body. If no proof has come for interpretation and specification, then saying both is saying something without evidence.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage addresses a secondary issue: once one affirms the reality of grave punishment, does it affect the soul alone or the soul together with the body? Buti first clarifies that differing on this specific question does not lead to kufr, because the decisive proofs only establish the original fact. The determination of its modality is subject to ijtihad. However, the position of Ahl al-Sunnah and the majority of Muslims is that punishment and bliss affect both soul and body together. Buti gives two reasons: (1) It is rationally possible, as already explained. (2) The apparent meaning (zahir) of the revealed texts indicates this, and there is no need for allegorical interpretation (ta'wil). He supports this with the famous hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: the Prophet addressed the dead polytheists at the well of Badr, calling them by name, and when 'Umar expressed amazement, the Prophet said that they hear just as the living do, though they cannot respond. Buti argues that if the bodies themselves were not the recipients of the address, the Prophet would not have spoken to them. A minority held that it is only for the soul. The majority responds that they have no proof for their specification and interpretation. Buti concludes logically: one who accepts the original reality for the soul can easily accept it for both soul and body. To insist on specification without proof is to speak without evidence.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
الروح
الجسد
التأويل
ظاهر النصوص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only the soul experiences grave punishment.
Correction: The Sunni view includes the body based on apparent scriptural evidence, such as the Prophet addressing the bodies of the dead at Badr.

Checkpoint
What is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah regarding the subject of grave punishment?
A) It is for the soul only
B) It is for the body only
C) It is for the soul and body together
D) It is not possible to know

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position is that grave punishment applies to both soul and body, based on the apparent meaning of texts and the Prophet's address to the dead of Badr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your body will experience the consequences of your deeds even before the resurrection, how would that change what you do with your body today? What specific habit will you change starting tomorrow?
?
When you read the Prophet's words to the dead of Badr, does it make you feel more accountable for your actions? Why or why not? Write down one action or thought you need to address because it will affect both your soul and body.
?
Is there an area of your life where you have assumed that only your soul matters, ignoring the physical actions you take? How will you correct that imbalance after this lesson? Commit to one concrete change.
