Dajjal's Deceptive Water and Fire
Buti cites a hadith about Dajjal's deceptive water and fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith about Dajjal's inversion of water and fire and the prophetic instruction to act against appearances.

Core Idea
Dajjal's deception inverts reality; faith sees through the illusion.

In this lesson, we examine a hadith that illustrates one of the major signs of the Hour: the Dajjal's deceptive use of water and fire. The Prophet ﷺ warns that what appears as water is actually fire, and what appears as fire is sweet water. This inversion tests the believer's obedience to revelation over sensory perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with Uqbah asking Hudhayfah to relate what he heard from the Prophet about the Dajjal.
Pay attention to the chain of narration: both Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Analyze the inversion
Identify the two pairs: apparent water is real fire, apparent fire is real water. Understand the purpose: the Dajjal creates an illusion to mislead people.
This inversion is a test of faith – will you trust your eyes or the Prophet's words?
3
Reflect on the command
Consider the Prophet's instruction: 'Let him fall into that which he sees as fire.' Why would he command such a counterintuitive action?
The command highlights that true knowledge comes from revelation, not from sensory experience.
4
Confirm the lesson
Note that Uqbah confirms he heard it too. This illustrates how the Companions preserved and verified prophetic teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
2 - روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن حذيفة ( واللفظ لمسلم ) أن عقبة قال له : حدثني ما سمعت من رسول الله صلى الله عليه في الدجال فقال : إن الدجال يخرج وإن معه ماء وناراً ، فأما الذي يراه الناس ماء فنار تحرق وأما الذي يراه الناس ناراً فماء بارد عذب ؛ فمن أدرك ذلك منكم فليقع في الذي يراه ناراً ، فإنه عذب طيب فقال عقبة : وأنا قد سمعته ، تصديقاً لحذيفة .
2 - The two Shaykhs and others narrated from Hudhayfah (the wording is from Muslim) that Uqbah said to him: Tell me what you heard from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about the Dajjal. He said: The Dajjal will emerge and with him will be water and fire. As for that which people see as water, it is fire that burns, and as for that which people see as fire, it is cool sweet water. So whoever among you reaches that time should fall into that which he sees as fire, for it is sweet and pure. Uqbah said: I too have heard it, confirming Hudhayfah.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a hadith from Hudhayfah (with wording from Muslim). It narrates that Uqbah asked Hudhayfah about what he heard from the Prophet concerning the Dajjal. Hudhayfah reports that the Dajjal will emerge accompanied by water and fire, but these are deceptive: what appears as water is actually burning fire, and what appears as fire is sweet, pure water. The Prophet instructs that whoever encounters this should jump into what appears as fire, because it is the real water. Uqbah then confirms that he too heard this from the Prophet, thus corroborating the report.

Key Terms
ماء
نار
دجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Dajjal's water and fire are literal and that one should avoid both.
Correction: The hadith explains they are inversions: the apparent water is fire, and the apparent fire is water. The Prophet commands to fall into what appears as fire, for it is sweet water. This is a test of faith.

Checkpoint

A) Avoid both.
B) Fall into what appears as fire.
C) Fall into what appears as water.
D) Wait for further instructions.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's deception inverts reality, but the believer follows revelation, not appearances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you chosen what felt good (sweet water) only to later realize it was burning fire because it contradicted Allah’s command? Will you jump into the 'fire' of obedience even when your senses scream otherwise?
?
The Dajjal will make evil look good and good look evil. What deceptions in today's world—social media, culture, peer pressure—are flipping truth and falsehood? Are you trusting your eyes or the Book of Allah?
?
Hudhayfah and Uqbah both testified to hearing this directly from the Prophet. Do you hold the revealed teachings with that same certainty, or do you water them down when they clash with your desires? Commit to one area today where you will obey Allah's words over your own judgment.

The Prophet's Description of the Dajjal
Hadith excerpt describing the Dajjal and giving instructions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Prophet's description of the Dajjal, including his appearance, the command to recite Surah al-Kahf, and where he will emerge.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is known by description; recite Surah al-Kahf as protection.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) warned his companions about the Dajjal with vivid detail. In this opening section of the hadith, he describes the Dajjal's physical traits, instructs believers on how to protect themselves, and reveals where the fitna will begin. This passage establishes the identity of the Dajjal and the first line of defense against him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Prophet's warning and description
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how the Prophet first addresses the companions' fear and then gives a detailed physical description of the Dajjal.
The Prophet compares the Dajjal to 'Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan, a known man of Quraysh.
2
Identify the protective measure
Find the specific instruction the Prophet gives to anyone who encounters the Dajjal. Reflect on why Surah al-Kahf is recommended.
3
Locate the emergence point
The Prophet states where the Dajjal will appear. This geographical detail is part of the fitna.
The 'gap' between Syria and Iraq is a known route.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's own stance
Consider why the Prophet says he is more afraid of other trials than the Dajjal. How does this shape the believer's mindset?
This shows that even a great trial like the Dajjal is not the ultimate danger – neglecting faith is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
3 - روى مسلم وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه وأحمد وغيرهم ، حديثاً طويلاً في شأن الدجال وما يكون في وقته نسوقه لك باختصار : عن النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه ، قال : ذكر رسول الله الله الدجال ذات غداة ، فخفض فيه ورفع ، حتى ظنناه في طائفة النخل (1) فلما رحنا إليه عرف ذلك فينا فقال : « غير الدجال أخوفني عليكم ، إن يخرج وأنا فيكم فأنا حجيجه دونكم ، وإن يخرج ولست فيكم فامرؤ حجيج نفسه . والله خليفتي على كل مسلم ، إنه شاب قطط عينه طافئة ، كأني أشبهه بعبد العزى بن قطن ، فمن أدركه منكم فليقرأ عليه فواتح سورة الكهف ، إنه خارج خلة بين الشام والعراق (2) فعاث يميناً وعاث شمالاً ، ياعباد الله فاثبتوا » . قلنا يا رسول الله وما لبثه في الأرض ؟ قال : « أربعون يوماً، يوم كسنة ويوم كشهر ، ويوم كجمعة ، وسائر أيامه كأيامكم » قلنا : يارسول الله فذلك اليوم الذي كسنة أتكفينا فيه صلاة يوم ؟ قال : « لا ، أقدروا له قدره » . قلنا : يارسول الله وما إسراعه في الأرض ؟ قال : « كالغيث استدبرته الريح فيأتي على القوم فيدعوهم فيؤمنون به ويستجيبون له فيأمر السماء فتمطر والأرض فتنبت . ثم يدعو رجلاً ممتلئاً شباباً فيضربه بالسيف فيقطعه جزلتين رمية الغرض ، ثم يدعوه فيقبل ويتهلل وجهه يضحك . فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين (1) واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين ، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر وإذا رفع تحدر منه مثل الجمان . فيطلبه ( أي يطلب الدجال ) حتى يدركه بباب لد (2) فيقتله (3) .
3 - Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ahmad and others narrated a long hadith concerning the Dajjal and what will happen in his time, which we present to you in summary: from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned the Dajjal one morning, speaking of him in a manner of varying emphasis, until we thought he was in a cluster of palm trees. (1) When we returned to him, he perceived that and said: 'Other than the Dajjal, I fear for you. If he emerges while I am among you, I will argue on your behalf; if he emerges while I am not among you, each person will argue for himself, and Allah is my successor over every Muslim. He is a young man with curly hair, his eye is blind, as if I compare him to Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. Whoever among you reaches him should recite the opening verses of Surah al-Kahf. He will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq (2) and will wreak havoc right and left. O servants of Allah, be steadfast.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his stay on earth? He said: 'Forty days: one day like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, on the day that is like a year, will one day's prayer suffice us? He said: 'No, estimate its due measure.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his speed on earth? He said: 'Like rain driven by the wind. He will come to a people and call them, they will believe in him and respond, and he will command the sky to rain and the earth to sprout. Then he will call a youth full of vitality, strike him with a sword and cut him into two pieces like a target, then call him and he will come forward with a beaming face laughing. While he is thus, Allah will send the Messiah, son of Mary, who will descend at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two garments (1), placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, beads like pearls fall. He will seek him (i.e., seek the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud (2) and kills him (3).'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a long hadith from several sources, summarized by the author. It begins with the Prophet's mention of the Dajjal, causing the companions to think he was nearby. The Prophet then lists several important points: 1) His greatest fear for the community is not the Dajjal but other trials; he instructs that if the Dajjal appears during his lifetime, he will personally argue; if not, each believer must argue for themselves. 2) He describes the Dajjal's appearance: a young man with curly hair and a blind eye, resembling Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. 3) He recommends reciting the opening of Surah al-Kahf as protection. 4) The Dajjal will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq. 5) His stay on earth will be forty days of varying lengths (like a year, month, week, then normal days); the Prophet clarifies that on the long day, prayers must be estimated. 6) His speed is compared to rain driven by wind. 7) He will perform apparent miracles: causing rain and vegetation, and killing a youth then reviving him. 8) Jesus (peace be upon him) will descend east of Damascus, wearing two garments, and will pursue the Dajjal to the gate of Lud and kill him. The footnotes explain the phrases: (1) 'in a cluster of palm trees' means they thought he was nearby; (2) 'gap' means a road; (1) on page 320 explains 'between two garments' as two yellow garments; (2) identifies Lud as a town in Palestine near Jerusalem; (3) refers to the full text in Muslim.

Key Terms
دجال
سورة الكهف

Key Terms from Source Passage

?

The Unusual Duration of the Dajjal's Stay
Hadith excerpt on the duration of the Dajjal's stay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique forty-day period of the Dajjal's rule, including the varying lengths of days and how prayers are to be estimated.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's days are not normal; prayer times must be estimated by proportion.

The companions asked about the length of the Dajjal's fitna. The Prophet's answer reveals that his stay will be forty days, but with days of unusual length—some like a year, a month, or a week. This passage clarifies how believers are to maintain their prayers during this extraordinary time.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer about duration
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the companions first ask about the length of stay, then about the day like a year.
2
Identify the four types of days
The Prophet lists four categories: a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, and the rest like normal days.
The order is important: one day equals a year, then a month, then a week, then normal.
3
Understand the prayer ruling
When asked about the day like a year, the Prophet does not suspend prayers but commands to estimate the times. Reflect on how this shows the importance of continuous worship.
This refutes a literal understanding of solar days; it's a period of trial with altered time perception.

3 - Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ahmad and others narrated a long hadith concerning the Dajjal and what will happen in his time, which we present to you in summary: from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned the Dajjal one morning, speaking of him in a manner of varying emphasis, until we thought he was in a cluster of palm trees. (1) When we returned to him, he perceived that and said: 'Other than the Dajjal, I fear for you. If he emerges while I am among you, I will argue on your behalf; if he emerges while I am not among you, each person will argue for himself, and Allah is my successor over every Muslim. He is a young man with curly hair, his eye is blind, as if I compare him to Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. Whoever among you reaches him should recite the opening verses of Surah al-Kahf. He will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq (2) and will wreak havoc right and left. O servants of Allah, be steadfast.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his stay on earth? He said: 'Forty days: one day like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, and the rest of his days like your days.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, on the day that is like a year, will one day's prayer suffice us? He said: 'No, estimate its due measure.' We said: O Messenger of Allah, what will be his speed on earth? He said: 'Like rain driven by the wind. He will come to a people and call them, they will believe in him and respond, and he will command the sky to rain and the earth to sprout. Then he will call a youth full of vitality, strike him with a sword and cut him into two pieces like a target, then call him and he will come forward with a beaming face laughing. While he is thus, Allah will send the Messiah, son of Mary, who will descend at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two garments (1), placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, beads like pearls fall. He will seek him (i.e., seek the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud (2) and kills him (3).'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a citation of a long hadith from several sources, summarized by the author. It begins with the Prophet's mention of the Dajjal, causing the companions to think he was nearby. The Prophet then lists several important points: 1) His greatest fear for the community is not the Dajjal but other trials; he instructs that if the Dajjal appears during his lifetime, he will personally argue; if not, each believer must argue for themselves. 2) He describes the Dajjal's appearance: a young man with curly hair and a blind eye, resembling Abd al-Uzza ibn Qatan. 3) He recommends reciting the opening of Surah al-Kahf as protection. 4) The Dajjal will emerge from a gap between Syria and Iraq. 5) His stay on earth will be forty days of varying lengths (like a year, month, week, then normal days); the Prophet clarifies that on the long day, prayers must be estimated. 6) His speed is compared to rain driven by wind. 7) He will perform apparent miracles: causing rain and vegetation, and killing a youth then reviving him. 8) Jesus (peace be upon him) will descend east of Damascus, wearing two garments, and will pursue the Dajjal to the gate of Lud and kill him. The footnotes explain the phrases: (1) 'in a cluster of palm trees' means they thought he was nearby; (2) 'gap' means a road; (1) on page 320 explains 'between two garments' as two yellow garments; (2) identifies Lud as a town in Palestine near Jerusalem; (3) refers to the full text in Muslim.

Key Terms
دجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the day like a year is a literal 365-day period where only one prayer is needed.
Correction: The Prophet's instruction to 'estimate its due measure' shows that it is not a literal solar day but a trial with altered time perception; all five daily prayers must still be observed by estimation.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about performing prayers on the day that is like a year?
A) It is sufficient to pray one fajr and one maghrib
B) Estimate the times for each prayer
C) No prayer is required on that day
D) Pray only the five obligatory prayers without Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's forty days include unusual lengths, but believers must estimate prayer times and maintain worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a period of darkness or confusion that seems endless (like a 'year-long day'), how do you ensure you still fulfill your obligations to Allah? Are you tempted to abandon or reduce your prayers because 'it's too long'? What does the Prophet's command 'estimate its measure' demand from you today?
?
The companions were concerned about prayer on an abnormally long day. Are you as vigilant about your prayers even when your schedule or circumstances feel unusual? What is one concrete change you can make to ensure you never miss a prayer, no matter how chaotic your day becomes?

The Miracles and Downfall of the Dajjal
Hadith excerpt on the Dajjal's miracles and his death by Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false miracles of the Dajjal, his speed, and the descent of Jesus to kill him, as described in the hadith.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's deceptive miracles are undone by the arrival of Jesus who kills him.

The hadith continues with the Dajjal's speed across the earth and his ability to perform apparent miracles like bringing rain, making vegetation grow, and reviving the dead. These deceptions will lead many astray until Jesus descends from heaven, catches him at the gate of Lud, and kills him. This passage lays out the final phase of the Dajjal's fitna and its conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read about the Dajjal's speed and miracles
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the comparison of his speed to rain driven by wind. Then identify the two false miracles: causing rain/vegetation and killing/reviving a youth.
2
Observe the reaction of the people
The Dajjal calls people and they believe. His miracles are convincing to those without faith.
3
Read about the descent of Jesus
Pay attention to the description of Jesus: his appearance, his location of descent (east of Damascus), and his mission to kill the Dajjal.
Jesus wears two yellow garments and has angels supporting him.
4
Reflect on the final defeat
The Dajjal is caught at the gate of Lud and killed. This ends his fitna.

The Distinctive Signs of the Dajjal
Buti relates Ibn Sayyad's story and enumerates Dajjal's signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinguishing signs of the Dajjal as described in the hadith and how they clarify confusion about his identity.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is identified by a set of specific signs, not by one trait alone.

This passage presents a historical anecdote about Ibn Sayyad, a figure suspected of being the Dajjal, followed by a summary of the authentic signs of the Dajjal from the hadith. The story shows how mere claims can be misleading, while the list of signs provides clear criteria for recognizing the Dajjal.

Guided Path
1
Read the story of Ibn Sayyad
Read the narration carefully to understand the context and his arguments against being the Dajjal.
Notice how Ibn Sayyad tries to refute the prophecies about the Dajjal.
2
Identify the contradiction
Ibn Sayyad claims to have done things the Dajjal cannot do: convert to Islam, have a child, and enter Mecca. Understand why this could cause confusion.
3
Examine the list of signs
Read the summary of the Dajjal's signs. List each sign mentioned: Jewish origin, emergence from east, blind right eye, no children, cannot enter Mecca/Medina, 'kafir' on forehead, killed by Jesus.
These signs are derived from multiple hadiths.
4
Reflect on the importance of multiple signs
Consider why having many signs is important: it prevents mistaken identity and clarifies that the Dajjal is a specific being with unique characteristics.
The story of Ibn Sayyad shows how even a convincing impostor can be ruled out by the full set of signs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
4 - وروى مسلم وغيره عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : قال لي ابن صائد واسمه صاف ، يهودي الأصل يمارس الكهانة ، كان يشاع في المدينة أنه ربما كان هو الدجال : مالي ومالكم يا أصحاب محمد ، ألم يقل نبي الله إنه يهودي وقد أسلمت ، وقال لا يولد له وقد ولد لي ، وقال إنه لا يدخل مكة وقد حججت . قال فما زال حتى كاد أن يأخذ في قوله . وهذا إن مجموع الأحاديث المختلفة الواردة في حقه ، تبين أنه ذو علامات فارقة كثيرة . فهو يهودي الأصل ، ويكون ظهوره من جهة المشرق ، على خلاف في البقعة المعينة التي يكون خروجه منها ، وعينه اليمنى عوراء جاحظة وطافية بشكل منكر ، ولا يولد له ولد ، ولا يُمكن من دخول مكة والمدينة ، مكتوب على جبهته ( كافر ) يتبينها كل مسلم ، ويقتله عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام .
4 - Muslim and others narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Ibn Sayyad, whose name was Saf, of Jewish origin, practicing divination, and it was rumored in Medina that he might be the Dajjal, said to me: What is wrong between me and you, O companions of Muhammad? Did not the Prophet of Allah say that he (the Dajjal) is Jewish, and I have become Muslim? He said he would have no children, and I have been given a child. He said he would not enter Mecca, and I have performed Hajj. He said: He kept going until he almost convinced him. And this is because the totality of the various hadiths narrated concerning him show that he has many distinguishing signs. He is of Jewish origin, his emergence will be from the east, though there is disagreement about the specific location. His right eye is blind, protuberant, and extremely ugly. He will have no children. He will not be able to enter Mecca and Medina. On his forehead is written 'kafir' (disbeliever), which every Muslim will discern. And Jesus, son of Mary (peace be upon him), will kill him.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage first narrates a hadith about Ibn Sayyad, a Jewish diviner who was suspected of being the Dajjal. He argued with Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, pointing out that some prophecies about the Dajjal did not apply to him: he had converted to Islam, had a child, and had performed Hajj, contradicting the hadith. The narrator says he almost convinced him. The author then comments that the collective hadiths about the Dajjal show many distinguishing signs. He lists them: the Dajjal is of Jewish origin; he emerges from the east; his right eye is blind and ugly; he has no children; he cannot enter Mecca and Medina; on his forehead is written 'kafir'; and he will be killed by Jesus (peace be upon him). This summary serves to clarify the true characteristics of the Dajjal, distinguishing him from impostors like Ibn Sayyad.

Key Terms
ابن صائد
يهودي الأصل
عينه اليمنى عوراء
مكتوب على جبهته كافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any one-eyed man or charismatic figure could be the Dajjal.
Correction: The Dajjal has a specific set of signs that include Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a blind right eye, childlessness, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'kafir' on his forehead, and being killed by Jesus. These signs together uniquely identify him.

Checkpoint

A) He is of Jewish origin.

C) He cannot enter Mecca or Medina.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is distinguished by a set of specific signs including Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a blind right eye, childlessness, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'kafir' on his forehead, and being killed by Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imagine you were in Medina when Ibn Sayyad was alive. His arguments seemed convincing—he converted, had a child, went to Hajj. Would you have been swayed? What does this teach you about the danger of judging by appearances instead of relying on the full prophetic description? How can you train yourself to trust the collective evidence of revelation over partial facts when evaluating truth claims in your own life?
?
The Dajjal's signs are specific and many. Yet many people today follow false prophets who exhibit only a few superficial traits. Where in your own heart do you find a tendency to accept a partial truth as the whole truth because it is comfortable or convenient? What habit can you adopt to ensure you seek the complete teaching of Islam before forming a conviction?

The Dajjal's Deceptions and the Descent of Jesus
Author recounts a hadith describing the Dajjal's miracles and Jesus' descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith describing the Dajjal's deceptive miracles and how Jesus will descend to kill him.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's miracles are tricks; only Jesus can stop him.

The author begins by presenting a prophetic hadith that vividly illustrates the Dajjal's powers and the ultimate intervention of Jesus. This story establishes the Dajjal as a deceptive figure whose apparent miracles are temporary and limited. Let's read the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the Dajjal's actions
Read the first part of the hadith describing how the Dajjal brings rain and vegetation, and kills and revives a man. Notice the deceptive nature of these acts.
These miracles are tests for believers.
2
Understand Jesus' descent
Read the description of Jesus' descent from heaven, including the specific location and his appearance. Note how he pursues and kills the Dajjal.
This emphasizes that only divine power can overcome the Dajjal.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the Prophet gave these details. The Dajjal's ability to mimic divine acts is part of his fitna, but his defeat is certain.

He said: 'Like a rain cloud driven by the wind, it comes upon a people, and he calls them, and they believe in him and respond to him. Then he commands the sky and it rains, and the earth and it grows. Then he calls a man full of youth, strikes him with a sword and cuts him into two pieces the distance of an arrow shot. Then he calls him, and he comes back with a shining face laughing. While he is like that, behold! Allah sends the Messiah, son of Mary. He descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two yellow garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, drops fall, and when he raises it, pearls like pearls trickle from him. He seeks him (i.e., seeks the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud and kills him.' And Muslim and others narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Ibn Sayyad [whose name is Saf, a Jew by origin, practiced soothsaying, it was rumored in Medina that he might be the Dajjal] said to me: 'What is between me and you, O companions of Muhammad? Did not the Prophet of Allah say that he is a Jew, and I have embraced Islam? He said he would have no children, and I have had a child. He said he would not perform Hajj, and I have performed Hajj?' He said: He kept on until he almost conceded to his statement. This, and all the various hadiths reported about him, show that he has many distinguishing signs. So he is of Jewish origin, his appearance will be from the east, with a difference of opinion about the precise location from which he will emerge. His right eye is blind, bulging, and floating in a hideous manner. He will have no children, he will not be allowed to enter Mecca and Medina, on his forehead is written 'Kafir' which every Muslim will discern, and Jesus son of Mary (peace be upon him) will kill him.

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths describing the Dajjal and a summary of his distinguishing signs. It begins with a lengthy hadith (attributed to someone, likely the Prophet) detailing the Dajjal's actions: he brings rain and vegetation, kills and revives a man, and then Jesus descends to kill him. The description of Jesus' descent includes specific details about the location (east of Damascus, at the white minaret) and his appearance. Then a second hadith is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri concerning Ibn Sayyad, a Jewish soothsayer rumored to be the Dajjal. The hadith records a conversation where Ibn Sayyad tries to refute the Prophet's predictions about the Dajjal's Jewishness, childlessness, and inability to perform Hajj. The passage then concludes with a list of the Dajjal's definitive signs synthesised from multiple hadiths: Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a deformed right eye, no children, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'Kafir' written on his forehead, and his death at the hands of Jesus. The passage thus serves to gather scriptural evidence about the Dajjal's identity and fate.

المسيح بن مريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Dajjal's power to revive the dead makes him a god or prophet.
Correction: The hadith shows his revival is a deceptive act; it is not true creation. Only Allah gives life, and Jesus, a prophet, kills him, proving his mortality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Dajjal's revival of the man was a trick—a laughing face hiding a lie. Is there any area of your life where you are laughing on the outside but spiritually dead inside? What would true resurrection look like for you, and are you willing to ask Jesus for it now?

The Distinguishing Signs of the Dajjal
Author presents a hadith about Ibn Sayyad and then lists the Dajjal's distinguishing signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the definitive signs of the Dajjal as synthesized from multiple hadiths.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's identity is unmasked by specific, unmistakable signs.

The author then presents a hadith about a historical figure (Ibn Sayyad) who was suspected to be the Dajjal, followed by a summary of the Dajjal's distinguishing signs compiled from various traditions. This lesson focuses on these signs and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ibn Sayyad incident
Read the hadith where Ibn Sayyad defends himself against allegations of being the Dajjal. Notice how he tries to refute the Prophet's predictions.
This shows that the Dajjal's signs are definitive and cannot be masked.
2
Identify the signs
Read the list of signs that follow. Each sign is a clear marker of the Dajjal's identity.
Count the signs: there are seven signs mentioned.
3
Memorize the signs
Try to commit these signs to memory. They are important for recognizing the Dajjal when he appears.
The signs include his origin, appearance, and limitations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : « كالغيث استدبرته الريح فيأتي على القوم فيدعوهم فيؤمنون به ، ويستجيبون له ، فيأمر السماء فتمطر والأرض فتنبت . ثم يدعو رجلاً ممتلئاً شباباً فیضربه بالسيف فيقطعه جزلتين رمية الغرض ، ثم يدعوه فيُقبل ويتهلل وجهه يضحك ؛ فبينما هو كذلك ! إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم ، فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مُهرودتين) واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين ، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر وإذا رفع تحدر منه مثل الجمان .. فيطلبه ) أي يطلب الدجال ) حتى يدركه بباب لد فيقتله . وروى مسلم وغيره عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال : قال لي ابن صائــد واسمه صاف ، يهودي الأصل يمارس الكهانة ، كان يشاع في المدينة أنه ربما كان هو الدجال : مالي ومالكم يا أصحاب محمد ، ألم يقل نبي الله إنه يهودي وقـد أسلمت ، وقال لا يولد له وقد ولد لي ، وقال إن حججت [؟] قال فما زال حتى كاد أن يأخذ في قوله [؟] هذا وإن مجموع الأحاديث المختلفة الواردة في حقه ، تبين أنه ذو علامات فارقة كثيرة . فهو يهودي الأصل ، ويكون ظهوره من جهة المشرق ، على خلاف في البقعة المعينة التي يكون خروجه منها ، وعينه اليمنى عوراء جاحظة وطافية بشكل منكر ، ولا يولد له ولد ، ولا يُمكن من دخول مكة والمدينة ، مكتوب على جبهته ( كافر ( يتبينها كل مسلم ، ويقتله عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام .
He said: 'Like a rain cloud driven by the wind, it comes upon a people, and he calls them, and they believe in him and respond to him. Then he commands the sky and it rains, and the earth and it grows. Then he calls a man full of youth, strikes him with a sword and cuts him into two pieces the distance of an arrow shot. Then he calls him, and he comes back with a shining face laughing. While he is like that, behold! Allah sends the Messiah, son of Mary. He descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two yellow garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels. When he lowers his head, drops fall, and when he raises it, pearls like pearls trickle from him. He seeks him (i.e., seeks the Dajjal) until he catches him at the gate of Lud and kills him.' And Muslim and others narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: Ibn Sayyad [whose name is Saf, a Jew by origin, practiced soothsaying, it was rumored in Medina that he might be the Dajjal] said to me: 'What is between me and you, O companions of Muhammad? Did not the Prophet of Allah say that he is a Jew, and I have embraced Islam? He said he would have no children, and I have had a child. He said he would not perform Hajj, and I have performed Hajj?' He said: He kept on until he almost conceded to his statement. This, and all the various hadiths reported about him, show that he has many distinguishing signs. So he is of Jewish origin, his appearance will be from the east, with a difference of opinion about the precise location from which he will emerge. His right eye is blind, bulging, and floating in a hideous manner. He will have no children, he will not be allowed to enter Mecca and Medina, on his forehead is written 'Kafir' which every Muslim will discern, and Jesus son of Mary (peace be upon him) will kill him.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of hadiths describing the Dajjal and a summary of his distinguishing signs. It begins with a lengthy hadith (attributed to someone, likely the Prophet) detailing the Dajjal's actions: he brings rain and vegetation, kills and revives a man, and then Jesus descends to kill him. The description of Jesus' descent includes specific details about the location (east of Damascus, at the white minaret) and his appearance. Then a second hadith is narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri concerning Ibn Sayyad, a Jewish soothsayer rumored to be the Dajjal. The hadith records a conversation where Ibn Sayyad tries to refute the Prophet's predictions about the Dajjal's Jewishness, childlessness, and inability to perform Hajj. The passage then concludes with a list of the Dajjal's definitive signs synthesised from multiple hadiths: Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a deformed right eye, no children, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'Kafir' written on his forehead, and his death at the hands of Jesus. The passage thus serves to gather scriptural evidence about the Dajjal's identity and fate.

ابن صائد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some thought Ibn Sayyad was the Dajjal.
Correction: The hadith shows Ibn Sayyad's claims did not match the true signs; thus the Dajjal is a future figure with clear markers.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a sign of the Dajjal according to the hadiths summarized?
A) He is of Jewish origin
B) His left eye is blind
C) He cannot enter Mecca and Medina
D) He is killed by Jesus

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is distinguished by seven clear signs: Jewish origin, emergence from the east, a deformed right eye, childlessness, inability to enter Mecca and Medina, 'Kafir' on his forehead, and death by Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Dajjal will appear with unmistakable signs, yet many will still follow him. What idols or deceptions in your own life have you allowed to go unchallenged despite clear warnings? Will you identify one today and actively turn away from it?
?
Ibn Sayyad used clever arguments to avoid being identified as the Dajjal. When you sin, do you rationalize or compare yourself to others to avoid repentance? What is the one excuse you need to abandon right now?
?
The Dajjal is barred from Mecca and Medina because of their sanctity. Do you truly honour these cities in your heart, or have you become careless about their status? What practical step can you take this week to increase your longing for them?

How Dajjal's 'Miracles' Differ from Prophetic Signs
Ibn Hajar answers an objection about Dajjal's miracles, using his defects to distinguish them from prophetic signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Dajjal's miracles, despite being stunning, do not prove his truthfulness, as they are accompanied by clear marks of falsehood and serve as a divine trial.

Core Idea
A miracle plus a mark of falsehood is a test, not a proof.

Ibn Hajar addresses a powerful objection: if the Dajjal can revive the dead, how can he be a liar? The answer reveals a key principle: a supposed miracle is not automatically a sign of truth when accompanied by undeniable signs of falsehood. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its implications for distinguishing prophetic miracles from mere wonders.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the passage where Ibn Hajar presents the objection about reviving the dead and then provides the answer. Notice the structure: a question followed by a clear rebuttal.
The objection is a common one - anyone can perform wonders seems truthful.
2
Identify the marks of falsehood
Ibn Hajar lists several defects: being one-eyed, 'Kafir' on the forehead, inability to remove his own flaws. List each and see how they contradict any claim to divinity.
3
Contrast with prophetic miracles
Prophetic miracles are free from such contradictions. Reflect on why a true prophet's miracles would not carry defects.
This contrast helps you see the logic behind the ruling.
4
Understand the purpose: trial
The answer emphasizes that these wonders are a fitna (trial). Consider why Allah would allow such signs for a false figure.
The trial lies in choosing between clear evidence (the marks) and dazzling events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ ابن حجر : فإن قلت كيف يُجري الله الآيات الباهرة على يده من مثل إحياء الموتى ، وهو من الآيات العظام التي لا تكون إلا للأنبياء ؟!.. فالجواب : إنه على سبيل الفتنة للعباد ، إذ كان عندهم ما يدل على أنـه مبطل غير محق في دعواه ، وهو أنه أعور مكتوب على جبهته كافر يقرؤه كل مسلم ، فدعواه داحضة ، مع وسم الكفر ونقص الذات والقدر ، إذ لو كان إلها لأزال ذلك عن وجهه ، وآيات الأنبياء سالمة عن المعارضة فلا يشتبهان .. ثم قال : وفي الدجال مع ذلك دلالة بينة ، لمن عقل ، على كذبه ، لأنه ذو أجزاء مؤلفة ، وتأثير الصنعة فيه ظاهر مع ظهور الآفة به من عور عينه ، فإذا دعا الناس إلى أنه ، فأسوأ حال من يراه من ذوي العقول أن يعلم أنه لم يكن ربهم ليسوّي خلق غيره ويعدله ويحسنه ، ولا يدفع النقص عن نفسه ، فأقل ما يجب أن يقول : يا من يزعم أنه خالق السماوات والأرض ، صور نفسك وعدلها ، وأزل عنها العاهة . فإن زعمت أن الربا لا يحدث في نفسه شيئاً ، فأزل ما هو مكتوب بين عينيك . قلت : وقد علمت أن الله عز وجل جعل ظهور الدجال ، فتنة خطيرة كبرى للناس ، كما بين الرسول مع الله وكما أنذر : ولو لم يكن قد مكنه الله من إحداث بعض الخوارق وجعل إليه مقاليد كثير من الخيرات والأرزاق ، لما كان فتنة إذا علمت هذا ، فاعلم أنه ليس للبحث العقلي أي سبيل إلى تحليل شخصية هذا الإنسان ودراسته ، من وراء هذا الذي أخبرت به النصوص الصحيحة . إذ إن المنفذ العقلي الوحيد إلى فهم أي شيء عنه إنما هو الخبر اليقيني ، ولولا ورود هذا الخبر لما تصورنا وجوده أصلاً فضلاً عن اعتقاده والإيمان بظهوره
Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: If you say: How does Allah manifest stunning signs at his hand such as reviving the dead, while these are among the great signs that occur only for prophets?! The answer: It is by way of trials for the servants, since they have evidence that he is false and not truthful in his claim. That is because he is one-eyed, written on his forehead is 'Kafir' which every Muslim reads. So his claim is null, along with the mark of disbelief and the defect in essence and power. For if he were a god, he would have removed that from his face. And the signs of prophets are free from contradiction, so they are not confused. Then he said: In the Dajjal, despite that, there is a clear proof for those who understand of his lying, because he is composed of parts, the effect of craftsmanship is apparent in him, and affliction is apparent in him from his blind eye. So when he calls people to [believe] that he is [god], the worst state for those of intellect who see him is that they know that he is not their lord, for he cannot create another being, nor balance and perfect it, nor remove defect from himself. The least that should be said is: O you who claim to be the creator of the heavens and the earth, form yourself and balance yourself, and remove the defect from yourself. If you claim that the Lord does not create anything in Himself, then remove what is written between your eyes. I say: You have known that Allah (Mighty and Majestic) made the emergence of the Dajjal a great and serious trial for people, as the Messenger informed from Allah and as he warned. If Allah had not empowered him to produce some miracles and placed in his hands many goods and provisions, he would not be a trial. Once you know this, know that rational inquiry has no way to analyze this man's character or study him beyond what the authentic texts have informed. For the only rational access to understanding anything about him is certain report (al-khabr al-yaqini). Were it not for this report, we would not have conceived of his existence at all, let alone believe in him and have faith in his emergence.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage contains an objection-and-answer format followed by the author's own commentary. First, Ibn Hajar raises a plausible objection: If the Dajjal performs stunning miracles like reviving the dead, which are usually only granted to prophets, how can he be an impostor? The answer is twofold: (1) These acts are a trial (fitna) for people, not a validation of truth. (2) The Dajjal bears unmistakable marks of falsehood: he is one-eyed, and 'Kafir' is written on his forehead for all Muslims to see. If he were a god, he would remove these defects. Prophetic miracles are not accompanied by such contradictions. Ibn Hajar then adds a rational proof: the Dajjal is a composite being with clear imperfections, so he cannot be the perfect creator. A rational person would challenge him to perfect his own form and remove his defect. The author (Ramadan Buti) then comments that the Dajjal is a great trial, and if he lacked miraculous powers, he would not be a trial. Finally, he asserts that rational inquiry cannot penetrate the nature of the Dajjal beyond what revelation states; the only valid source of knowledge here is authentic prophetic report (al-khabr al-yaqini). Without that report, we would not even know of his existence. Thus the passage defends the compatibility of miracles with falsehood in the context of divine trial and emphasizes the supremacy of revelation over reason in eschatological matters.

Key Terms
الآيات الباهرة
الفتنة
الدجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any supernatural event proves the person is truthful and from God.
Correction: A miracle is only a sign of truth when it is free from contradictions and accompanying marks of falsehood, as Ibn Hajar explains. The Dajjal's case shows that wonders can be a trial, not a proof.

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason Ibn Hajar gives for why Dajjal's miracles do not prove his truthfulness?
A) The miracles are not real; they are illusions
B) The Dajjal's miracles are not witnessed by many people
C) The Dajjal bears visible defects and a mark of disbelief
D) The Dajjal's miracles cause harm instead of benefit

Key Takeaway
A miracle is not automatically a sign of truth; it must be free from accompanying marks of falsehood to be considered a prophetic sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone claiming to have spiritual gifts or signs from Allah, do you examine their character for marks of falsehood, or are you easily impressed by outward wonders? What defect would you overlook in yourself that disproves your own authority?
?
The Dajjal's miracles will be breathtaking, yet the test is to reject them based on clear signs of falsehood. If you were faced with such a spectacle, would your love for the truth overcome your desire for the miraculous?
?
Ibn Hajar points out that the Dajjal cannot even perfect his own form. How often do you claim knowledge or leadership while failing to remove the obvious 'defects' between your own eyes—your unchecked pride, anger, or hypocrisy? What is the one defect you must remove today?

The Limits of Rational Inquiry: Dajjal and Revelation
Author Buti concludes that rational inquiry cannot penetrate the Dajjal's reality; only certain reports from revelation provide knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational inquiry cannot analyze the Dajjal's nature or existence beyond what is revealed in authentic texts, and why certain reports (khabar yaqini) are the only valid source of knowledge here.

Core Idea
Reason cannot access what revelation alone brings.

After establishing that the Dajjal's miracles are a trial, the author (Ramadan Buti) draws a crucial methodological conclusion: the Dajjal, as an eschatological figure, cannot be studied through rational inquiry. The only path to knowledge about him is through certain reports from revelation (al-khabr al-yaqini). This lesson explores why reason hits its limit and why submission to revelation is necessary in such matters.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of Dajjal's miracles
The author states that the Dajjal would not be a trial without his miraculous powers. Reflect on this: the trial includes both the wonders and the clear evidence of falsehood.
This sets the stage for why reason is insufficient.
2
Identify the limit of reason
The author explicitly says 'rational inquiry has no way to analyze this man's character or study him beyond what the authentic texts have informed.' Find this statement and see how it limits our tools.
3
Understand the role of certain report
The only 'rational access' is through al-khabr al-yaqini. Consider what makes a report certain in Islamic epistemology.
This is not a rejection of reason but an acknowledgment of its boundaries.
4
Apply the principle
Without revelation, we would not even know of the Dajjal's existence. Ask yourself: what other doctrines depend solely on revelation?
This principle applies to all sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation).

?

Is there an area of your life—maybe your career, relationships, or future—where you are trying to rely solely on your own reasoning instead of turning to what Allah has revealed? What would it look like to trust the 'certain report' over your own calculations starting today?
?
If the only way to know about the Dajjal is through Allah's revelation, what does that say about your daily need for the Qur'an and Sunnah? Will you commit to spending a specific time this week studying the relevant texts instead of speculating?
?
The author describes the Dajjal as a 'great trial' precisely because he has miraculous powers that could deceive people. In your own life, what 'miracles' or impressive worldly successes might be trials that distract you from the truth revealed by Allah? How can you ensure that you evaluate everything—even seemingly good things—by the standard of revelation rather than rational appeal?

Ibn Hajar's Refutation of the Dajjal's Divinity
Ibn Hajar refutes the Dajjal's claim to divinity using physical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Hajar's rational argument that the Dajjal's physical defects and composite nature disprove his claim to divinity, despite his apparent miracles.

Core Idea
Physical flaws expose the Dajjal's false divinity – a god cannot be imperfect.

Ibn Hajar addresses a critical question: if the Dajjal performs miracles like reviving the dead, how can his claim to divinity be false? He responds with a twofold argument from physical evidence: the Dajjal's one eye and the word 'kafir' on his forehead are clear signs of imperfection that no god would tolerate, and his composite nature proves he is created. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Ibn Hajar begins with an imagined objection: 'How can God allow such great miracles at the hand of the Dajjal?'
The objection is a common one – miracles seem to confirm truth.
2
Examine the first answer: the defects disprove divinity
Ibn Hajar answers that the miracles are a test (fitna), but the clear defects (being one-eyed and having 'kafir' written) show the Dajjal is false. A god would remove these imperfections.
The word 'dahida' means invalid, completely false.
3
Understand the second argument: composite nature
The Dajjal is composed of parts, showing he is created. A creator cannot be created. The effect of craftsmanship is evident in his body, and he cannot remove his own defects.
This argument relies on the principle that what is composite needs a maker.
4
Reflect on the lesson's takeaway
Consider how this argument protects believers from being deceived by false miracles. The presence of clear indicators of falsehood (defects) alongside miracles shows the miracles are a test, not a certification of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحافظ ابن حجر : فإن قلت كيف يُجري الله الآيات الباهرة على يده من مثل إحياء الموتى ، وهو من الآيات العظام التي لا تكون إلا للأنبياء ؟!.. فالجواب : إنه على سبيل الفتنة للعباد ، إذ كان عندهم ما يدل على أنه مبطل غير محق في دعواه ، وهو أنه أعور مكتوب على جبهته كافر يقرؤه كل مسلم ، فدعواه داحضة ، مع وسم الكفر ونقص الذات والقدر ، إذ لو كان إلها لأزال ذلك عن وجهه ، وآيات الأنبياء سالمة عن المعارضة فلا يشتبهان .. ثم قال : وفي الدجال مع ذلك دلالة بينة ، لمن عقل ، على كذبه ، لأنه ذو أجزاء مؤلفة ، وتأثير الصنعة فيه ظاهر مع ظهور الآفة به من عور عينه ، فإذا دعا الناس إلى أنه ، فأسوأ حال من يراه من ذوي العقول أن يعلم أنه لم يكن ربهم ليسوي خلق غيره ويعدله ويحسنه ، ولا يدفع النقص عن نفسه ، فأقل ما يجب أن يقول : يا من يزعم أنه خالق السماوات والأرض ، صور نفسك وعدلها ، وأزل عنها العاهة . فإن زعمت أن الرب لا يحدث في نفسه شيئاً ، فأزل ما هو مكتوب بين عينيك
Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: If you say, 'How does God bring about manifest miracles at his hand, such as reviving the dead, which are among the great miracles that occur only for prophets?' The answer: It is as a trial (fitna) for the servants, since they have something that indicates that he is false and not truthful in his claim – namely, that he is one-eyed and written on his forehead is 'kafir' which every Muslim reads. So his claim is invalid, along with the brand of disbelief and the deficiency of essence and power. For if he were a god, he would remove that from his face. The miracles of prophets are safe from opposition, so they are not confused. Then he said: In the Dajjal, moreover, there is a clear indication, for one who understands, of his falsehood, because he is composed of parts and the effect of craftsmanship is apparent in him, along with the appearance of defect upon him from the blindness of his eye. So if he calls people to claim divinity, the worst state of one who sees him among the intelligent is that he knows that he is not their Lord who creates others, and equalizes and perfects them, and does not remove defect from himself. The least one should say is: 'O you who claim to be the Creator of the heavens and the earth, form yourself and perfect it, and remove the defect from it.' For if you claim that the Lord does not bring about anything in Himself, then remove what is written between your eyes.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof: Ibn Hajar refutes the claim that the Dajjal could be divine despite performing apparent miracles. He quotes an imaginary objector who asks how God could allow such miracles through a false claimant. The answer is that these miracles are a test (fitna), not a certification of truth, because there are clear indicators of falsehood: the Dajjal is one-eyed and the word 'kafir' is visibly written on his forehead for every Muslim to read. These defects prove his claim is 'dahida' (false). If he were a god, he would have removed these imperfections. Prophetic miracles are never accompanied by such contradictions. Ibn Hajar then adds a second argument: the Dajjal's composite nature (having parts) and the obvious effect of craftsmanship on him, along with his physical defect, demonstrate that he cannot be the Creator. Any intelligent person would see that he is not the Lord who perfectly creates others yet cannot perfect himself. The minimal response to his claim is a demand: if you claim to be the Creator, perfect your own form and remove your defect. If you argue that the Lord does not cause change in Himself, then change what is written on your forehead — but he cannot. Thus his claim is self-refuting.

Key Terms
الدجال
الآيات الباهرة
الفتنة
أعور
كافر
داحضة
ذو أجزاء مؤلفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Dajjal's miracles (like reviving the dead) prove that his claim to divinity is true.
Correction: Ibn Hajar shows that the Dajjal's physical defects (one eye, written 'kafir') and his composite nature are clear indicators that he is false. Miracles can be a test, not a certification of truth.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Hajar, what is the primary evidence that the Dajjal is not divine despite performing miracles?
A) His miracles are weak and unconvincing.
B) He has physical defects that a god would remove.
C) The Quran declares him a liar.
D) He admits he is a liar.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's physical defects and composite nature are definitive proof that he is not divine; a true god would be free from imperfection and need no creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Hajar says the Dajjal's defects expose his falsehood. What defects in your own character are you aware of but have been ignoring, allowing them to contradict your claim to something you are not?
?
If you were to demand of yourself, 'Form yourself and perfect it, and remove the defect from yourself,' what one defect would you be most ashamed to face? Will you begin today to remove it, or will you remain like the Dajjal, unable to change?
?
The Dajjal's miracles were a trial. Think of a 'miracle' or blessing in your life that could become a test for you—something that makes you feel self-sufficient. Are you using it to draw closer to Allah or to feed your ego?

The Descent of Jesus: A Major Sign of the Hour
Buti defines the descent of Jesus and its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of Jesus's descent as one of the major signs of the Hour, his current state of concealment, and his role in establishing the Islamic creed and implementing Islamic Sharia.

Core Idea
Jesus will descend to implement the final Islamic Sharia, not a new law.

This lesson examines a key eschatological event: the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him). It clarifies where Jesus is now, why he will descend, and what he will do. As you read, note that the passage emphasizes that Jesus will uphold the same Islamic creed all prophets proclaimed and will enforce the Islamic Sharia that supersedes all earlier laws.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to key terms like نزول عيسى, أشراط الساعة, الاحتجاب, ملكوت الله, الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة.
The Arabic text is continuous; notice the flow from definition to purpose.
2
Identify the two purposes of Jesus's descent
The passage mentions two main tasks: establishing the pillars of the Islamic creed and implementing the Islamic Sharia that abrogates previous laws. Find these in the text.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is this event considered one of the most important and dangerous signs of the Hour? How does it affirm Jesus's prophethood and the finality of Islamic law?
This connects to the broader Islamic eschatological narrative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲ - نزول عيسى ابن مريم : وهو من أهم أشراط الساعة ، ومن أخطر الأحداث التي تكون بين يديها ومعنى نزوله ، أنه يهبط إلى الأرض ، بعد احتجابه عنها كل هذه الحقبة الطويلة من الدهر ، في مكان ما من ملكوت الله عز وجل ، وهو لا يزال يتمتع بحياته الأولى التي أحياه الله بها إذ كان في الأرض رسولاً نبياً . فيمكث في الأرض مدة من الزمن يقيم عليها دعائم العقيدة الإسلامية التي بعث هو والأنبياء كلهم لإقامتها ، وينفذ الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة لجميع الشرائع السابقة والتي بعث بها
2 – The descent of Jesus son of Mary: It is one of the most important signs of the Hour and one of the most dangerous events that occur during its approach. The meaning of his descent is that he will descend to earth, after being concealed from it throughout this long period of time, from some place in the dominion (malkut) of God, Mighty and Majestic, while he still enjoys his first life with which God gave him life when he was on earth as a messenger and prophet. He will remain on earth for a period of time, establishing upon it the pillars of the Islamic creed which he and all the prophets were sent to establish, and he will implement the Islamic Sharia that abrogates all previous laws and which was sent.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the descent of Jesus (Isa ibn Maryam) as a major eschatological event. The author states it is one of the most important signs of the Hour and one of the most dangerous events preceding it. The meaning of 'nuzul' (descent) is that Jesus will physically descend to earth after having been concealed (ihtijab) from it for a very long period. He is currently in some location within God's dominion (malkut), still alive with the same life he had on earth as a messenger and prophet. Upon descending, he will stay for a time, establishing the foundations of the Islamic creed — the same creed all prophets came to establish — and he will implement the Islamic Sharia which abrogates all previous laws. This passage clarifies the nature and purpose of Jesus' second coming within Islamic eschatology.

Key Terms

أشراط الساعة
الاحتجاب
ملكوت الله
الشريعة الإسلامية
الناسخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Jesus will bring a new law or scripture when he returns.
Correction: The passage explicitly says he will implement the existing Islamic Sharia that abrogates all previous laws, not a new revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what will Jesus do after he descends?
A) He will bring a new scripture.
B) He will establish the pillars of Islamic creed and implement Islamic Sharia.
C) He will judge all of humanity immediately.
D) He will fight alongside the Dajjal.

Key Takeaway
Jesus will descend from a place in God's dominion, still alive, to establish the Islamic creed and implement the final Sharia that abrogates all previous laws.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Jesus will descend to implement the exact same Islamic Sharia we have today, how seriously are you currently taking your own obedience to that Sharia? What is one specific command of Allah that you have been neglecting, and what will you change today?
?
The descent of Jesus is described as one of the most dangerous events before the Hour. Does your heart truly recognize the gravity of the Hereafter, or have you become numb to reminders? What will you do today to revive your fear of Allah?
?
Jesus will establish the pillars of the Islamic creed. Do you find that your own belief in those pillars is firm and active? Which pillar do you feel weakest in, and what step will you take this week to strengthen it?

The Wisdom of Not Naming the Dajjal in the Quran
Answers why the Dajjal is not named in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Dajjal's name is not mentioned in the Quran and how this reflects Allah's wisdom and the Quran's stylistic pattern.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in Allah's eternal speech.

An objection is raised: if the Dajjal is such a major figure of the end times, why is he not named in the Quran? In this passage, the author provides a two-part answer: first, the Dajjal is too insignificant for his name to be recorded in the Quran; second, the Quran's pattern is to only name prophets and some tyrants they were sent to. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the first part of the passage from 'والجواب' to 'بالذكر والتعيين' to see the two reasons given.
2
Reflect on the concept of hikmah
Consider why the author emphasizes that the Dajjal is 'ahwan' (more insignificant) in Allah's sight. What does this teach about Allah's majesty?
3
Compare with Quranic pattern
Notice the author's point about the Quran's general style of not naming individuals except prophets and some tyrants. How does this support the answer?
This is a common feature of Quranic narratives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب : إنه لا يبعد أن تكون الحكمة ذلك أن الدجال أهون على الله من أن يسجل اسمه في كتابه وكلامه القديم، يتلى على ألسنة الناس في كل زمان ومكان . وقد درج القرآن في أسلوبه وإخباراته على عدم ذكر الأسماء - اللهم إلا أسماء الرسل والأنبياء - وبعض الطغاة الذين أرسلوا إليهم . أفيخص الدجال وحده بالذكر والتعيين ؟! .. ومهما يكن فإن الخبر الصادق الذي يتحتم الاعتقاد بموجبه ليس محصوراً في القرآن فقط ، بل هو كما يكون في القرآن يكون في السنة أيضاً ، إذا وصل إلينا بطرق صحيحة متواترة وقد شاعت أخيراً ( تقليعة ( بين بعض المتفيقهين المنافقين الذين يظهرون ما لا يبطنون وهي أن أحدهم يمسك بحكم من أحكام الشريعة المجمع عليها ، ثم يطالبك أن تأتيه بنص عليه في القرآن : والقرآن فقط ، وإلا فهو لا يعتد به ! ..
وهو
ومن أجل هذا فإنك تجد الواحد منهم يسأل مثل هذه الأسئلة لا يؤدي صلاة ولا صوماً ولا يلتزم شعيرة من شعائر الإسلام. إذ كان عذره أن القرآن لم يترح له كيفية الصلاة والصيام وبقية الأحكام ! .. ومقتضى منطق هؤلاء أن يتركوا القرآن الذي تنزل على محمد الله ، ولا يعتمدوا إلا على قرآن ينزل على كل منهم مباشرة ، فذلك أقطع للشك وأنفى للريبة
The answer: It is not far that the wisdom is that the Dajjal is too insignificant in the sight of Allah for his name to be recorded in His book and His ancient speech, to be recited on the tongues of people at all times and places. The Quran has been accustomed in its style and reports to not mentioning names - except for the names of messengers and prophets - and some of the tyrants to whom they were sent. Should the Dajjal be singled out for mention and specification?! ... However, the truthful report which it is obligatory to believe is not confined to the Quran only, but just as it is in the Quran, it is also in the Sunnah, if it reaches us through authentic and mutawatir chains. Recently a trend has spread among some hypocritical pseudo-faqihs who show what they do not conceal, which is that one of them holds onto a ruling of the Sharia that is unanimously agreed upon, then demands that you bring him a text for it in the Quran: only the Quran, otherwise he does not consider it! ... For this reason, you find one of them asking such questions, not performing prayer or fasting or adhering to any ritual of Islam, because his excuse is that the Quran did not mention for him the method of prayer, fasting, and the rest of the rulings! ... The logic of these people requires that they abandon the Quran which was revealed to Muhammad, and rely only on a Quran revealed to each of them directly, for that is more conclusive for doubt and more repelling of suspicion.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer. The objection, implied, is why the Dajjal is not mentioned by name in the Quran. The author's answer gives two reasons: first, the Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in the eternal speech; second, the Quran's style is not to mention names except for prophets and some tyrants. Then the author expands to a broader principle: the 'truthful report' (al-khabr al-sadiq) that must be believed is not limited to the Quran but includes the Sunnah when authentically and mutawatirly transmitted. This leads to a critique of a recent trend among hypocritical pseudo-jurists who demand a Quranic text for every sharia ruling, rejecting hadith entirely. The author exposes the absurdity of their position by noting that even basic obligations like prayer and fasting have their detailed methods described not in the Quran but in the Sunnah. He concludes that such logic would force them to abandon the Quran and seek a personal revelation, which is absurd.

Key Terms
الدجال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the Dajjal not named in the Quran?
A) Because the Quran only names prophets and angels.
B) Because the Dajjal is too insignificant and the Quran's style is to rarely name individuals.
C) Because the Dajjal's name is too sacred.
D) Because the Dajjal will appear in the future.

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal is not named in the Quran because of his insignificance and the Quran's general pattern of not naming individuals except prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Dajjal is too insignificant to be named in Allah's eternal speech, how does that change the weight you give to your own fears and trials? Will you today recite a verse that reminds you of Allah's greatness whenever you feel overwhelmed?
?
The Quran only names prophets and their adversaries. Where do you see yourself in that divide? Take a moment to sincerely repent if you find your heart inclining towards the ways of the tyrants.
?
What is one specific fear about the future that you need to surrender to Allah right now, realizing it may be trivial in His sight? Write it down and commit to relying on Him alone.

The Authority of the Sunnah and the Refutation of the Quran-Only Trend
Asserts the authority of the Sunnah and refutes the Quran-only trend.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sunnah is an equally binding source of religious obligations when authentically transmitted, and the fallacy of rejecting it.

Core Idea
The truthful report is not limited to the Quran; the Sunnah is also binding.

The author moves from the specific case of Dajjal to a broader methodological issue. He asserts that the 'truthful report' (al-khabr al-sadiq) includes the Sunnah when transmitted via authentic and mutawatir chains. Then he critiques a contemporary trend of people who claim to follow the Quran alone and reject hadith, highlighting the absurdity by noting that the Quran itself does not detail the methods of prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read from 'ومهما يكن' to the end to understand the authority of Sunnah and the critique of Quran-only trend.
2
Understand 'khabar sadiq'
The author explains that the 'truthful report' which must be believed is not only in the Quran but also in the Sunnah if it reaches us via authentic mutawatir chains. Why is mutawatir important?
Mutawatir means transmitted by so many narrators that collusion on a lie is impossible.
3
Reflect on the critique
The author uses strong language to describe those who demand Quranic text for every ruling, calling them hypocrites and pseudo-faqihs. Why does he say their logic would force them to seek a personal Quran?
Because the Quran does not detail the methods of prayer, fasting, etc., so their position is self-defeating.

The Descent of Jesus and Its Implications
Defines the descent of Jesus and clarifies it does not contradict Muhammad's finality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of Jesus' descent, its purpose, and why it does not contradict Muhammad being the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
Jesus returns to implement Muhammad's law, not to bring a new one.

One of the major signs of the Hour is the descent of Jesus. This passage from al-Buti explains its meaning and addresses a common concern: does it conflict with the finality of prophethood? Let's see how the author answers this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the key components
Notice that the passage defines the descent, states its purpose, and then addresses a potential objection regarding Muhammad's finality.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يناقض' (does not contradict).
3
Understand the argument
The author argues that Jesus descends to implement the Islamic Sharia without new revelation, so it does not contradict Muhammad being the final prophet.
This is a common point of confusion that the passage clarifies.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this doctrine is important for Islamic eschatology and how it reinforces the finality of Muhammad's prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ - نزول عيسى ابن مريم :
،
وهو من أهم أشراط الساعة ، ومن أخطر الأحداث التي تكون بين يديها ومعنى نزوله ، أنه يهبط إلى الأرض ، بعد احتجابه عنها كل هذه الحقبة الطويلة من الدهر ، في مكان ما من ملكوت الله عز وجل ، وهو لا يزال يتمتع بحياته الأولى التي أحياه الله بها إذ كان في الأرض رسولاً نبياً . فيمكث في الأرض مدة من الزمن يقيم عليها دعائم العقيدة الإسلامية التي بعث هو والأنبياء كلهم لإقامتها ، وينفذ الشريعة الإسلامية الناسخة لجميع الشرائع السابقة والتي بعث بها
محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، دون أن يؤيد خلال ذلك بوحي جديد من الله عز وجل .
وبذلك تعلم أن نزوله ، لا يناقض كون محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام هو خاتم الأنبياء وآخرهم ، كما لا يناقض أن شريعته ناسخة لجميع الشرائع وباقية إلى يوم القيامة .
2 - The Descent of Jesus Son of Mary: It is one of the most important signs of the Hour, and one of the most dangerous events that occur before it. The meaning of his descent is that he descends to the earth, after being concealed from it for this long period of time, in a place from the dominion of Allah Almighty, while he still enjoys his first life which Allah granted him when he was on earth as a messenger and prophet. He will remain on earth for a period of time to establish the foundations of the Islamic creed which he and all the prophets were sent to establish, and he will implement the Islamic Sharia which abrogates all previous laws, and which was sent with Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, without being supported during that by a new revelation from Allah Almighty. Thus you know that his descent does not contradict that Muhammad is the Seal of the Prophets and the last of them, just as it does not contradict that his Sharia abrogates all previous laws and remains until the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage defines the descent of Jesus (nuzul 'Isa) and explains its significance. It begins by identifying it as a major sign of the Hour. The author then explains the meaning: Jesus will physically descend to earth after a long period of concealment, still alive in his original human life. His purpose is to establish the Islamic creed and implement the Islamic Sharia (shari'a islamiyya) that abrogates all previous laws, the same Sharia sent with Muhammad. Importantly, Jesus will not bring new revelation; he follows Muhammad's law. The author then directly addresses a potential objection: this does not contradict Muhammad being the Seal of the Prophets (khatam al-anbiya') or the finality of his Sharia. Thus, the descent is not a new prophetic mission but a reaffirmation of the existing message.

Key Terms
نزول عيسى
أشراط الساعة
خاتم الأنبياء
شريعة ناسخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe Jesus' descent implies he brings a new law or contradicts Muhammad's finality.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Jesus descends to implement the existing Islamic Sharia without new revelation, so it does not contradict Muhammad being the final prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of the descent of Jesus?
A) He will come as a new prophet with a new revelation.
B) He will descend to earth still alive and implement the Islamic Sharia.
C) He will abrogate the Sharia of Muhammad.
D) He will be born again.

Key Takeaway
The descent of Jesus reaffirms the Islamic creed and Sharia without contradicting Muhammad's finality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Jesus will descend exactly as described in this lesson? If you are certain, how does that certainty affect the way you live today?
?
If Jesus were to descend today, would you be following the same Sharia he will implement? Examine your daily life: where do you fall short?
?
The passage emphasizes that Jesus will not bring new revelation. Does your heart fully accept that Islam is complete and final? What might you be unknowingly seeking outside of it?
