The Major Signs of the Hour
Al-Buti enumerates ten major eschatological signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the list of major signs of the Hour as enumerated by Al-Buti, including the Smoke, Dajjal, Beast, and others.

Core Idea
Ten major signs precede the Hour, ending with a fire from Yemen.

Al-Buti begins by listing the major signs of the Hour, starting with the Smoke and ending with the fire that drives people to their gathering. This enumeration sets the eschatological context for the detailed discussion of each sign, especially the descent of Jesus.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the list of signs in Arabic and English. Notice the order: from cosmic signs to geographical sinkings to the final fire.
2
Identify each sign
Make a mental note of each sign: Smoke, Dajjal, Beast, sun rising from west, descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three sinkings, and the fire.
3
Reflect on the classification
Consider that these are the 'major' signs, distinct from minor signs. Al-Buti does not discuss minor signs here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدخان، والدجال، والدابة، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، ونزول عيسى بن مريم، ويأجوج ومأجوج، وثلاثة خسوف: خسف بالمشرق، وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم. ٣ - ما رويناه آنفاً عن مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي وأحمد وابن ماجه من حديث النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه عن رسول الله، بشأن الدجال، وفيه: فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم، فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر، وإذا رفعه تحدر منه جمان كاللؤلؤ، فلا يحل لكافر يجد ريح نفسه إلا مات، ونفسه ينتهي حيث ينتهي طرفه فيطلبه حتى يدركه بباب لد فيقتله ثم يأتي عيسى قوم قد عصمهم الله منه، فيمسح عن وجوههم ويحدثهم بدرجاتهم في الجنة ... الحديث ٤ - ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود وابن جرير بطرق مختلفة عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله: «الأنبياء إخوة لعلات، أمهاتهم شتى ودينهم واحد، صلى الله عليه وسلم وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه، رجل مربوع، إلى الحمرة والبياض، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل: فيدق الصليب، ويقتل الخنزير، ويضع الجزية، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام، ويهلك المسيح الدجال، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله، من رواية أبي هريرة، وابن مسعود، وعثمان بن أبي العاص، وأبي أمامة، والنواس بن سمعان، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
The Smoke, and the Dajjal, and the Beast, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus son of Mary, and Gog and Magog, and three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that comes out of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place. 3 - What we related previously from Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and Ibn Majah from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Messenger of Allah, concerning the Dajjal, and in it: 'While he is thus, Allah sends the Messiah son of Mary, and he descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two dyed garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels; when he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, drops fall from it like pearls; no disbeliever who smells his breath dies but he dies, and his breath reaches as far as his sight reaches; so he pursues him until he catches him at the gate of Ludd and kills him. Then Jesus comes to a people whom Allah has protected from him, and he wipes their faces and tells them of their ranks in Paradise... the hadith.' 4 - What Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Jarir narrated through various chains from Abu Hurayra, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The prophets are paternal brothers; their mothers are different but their religion is one. And I am the nearest of people to Jesus son of Mary because there was no prophet between me and him, and he will descend. When you see him, recognize him: a man of medium height, reddish-white, wearing two light-yellow garments, his head as if it is dripping though no moisture touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, impose the jizya, and call people to Islam. Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and he will destroy the Dajjal. Then he will remain on earth for forty years, then he will die, and the Muslims will pray over him.' So these are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary. There are many other hadiths which cannot be enumerated here. The summary is that they are hadiths of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Messenger of Allah, narrated by Abu Hurayra, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Usayd, may Allah be pleased with them all. And before that, we have examined the definitive verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same as these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have achieved consensus (ijma') on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His decisive declaration.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument that begins with a classification of the major signs of the Hour, then focuses on the descent of Jesus as one of those signs, provides two detailed hadiths as proofs, and concludes with the affirmation of the doctrine based on tawatur and ijma'. The author first enumerates ten major events: the Smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three land sinkings (east, west, and Arabian Peninsula), and finally a fire from Yemen that drives people to their gathering place. This enumeration sets the eschatological context. Then he presents a lengthy hadith from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, which describes the Dajjal and Jesus' descent at the white minaret east of Damascus, his killing of the Dajjal at the gate of Ludd, and his care for the believers. The second hadith from Abu Hurayra emphasizes Jesus' role in breaking the cross, killing pigs, abolishing jizya, and calling to Islam, and states that he will remain on earth forty years. The author then asserts that these two hadiths, along with two others mentioned but not quoted, constitute a body of mutawatir (mass transmitted) reports, listing multiple companions as narrators. He further appeals to Quranic verses (unquoted) as supporting evidence and declares that the Muslims have reached consensus (ijma') on the literal bodily descent of Jesus at the end of time, confirming his bodily ascension. Thus, the passage establishes the doctrine through textual proof (hadith and Qur'an) and communal consensus, refuting any metaphorical interpretation.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
الدجال
المسيح الدجال
نزول عيسى
خسف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the major signs are only a few events, but this list shows ten distinct signs.
Correction: Al-Buti's enumeration includes ten signs, and each is a separate major event.

Checkpoint
How many sinkings (خسوف) are mentioned?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hour is preceded by ten major signs, including the Dajjal, Jesus' descent, and the fire from Yemen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Smoke is described as a sign that will suffocate the disbelievers. If you saw the sky filled with such smoke tonight, would you be among those who recognize it and repent, or would you be among the heedless? What is holding you back from turning to Allah fully right now?
?
The Beast will speak to people and distinguish believers from disbelievers. Do you have certainty in all the unseen matters of the Hour, including this sign? Is there any doubt in your heart that you need to remove by seeking knowledge and strengthening your faith?
?
The last sign is a fire that will drive all of humanity to their gathering place. Imagine that fire behind you, pushing you forward. Are you living today as if you will face that gathering with faith and good deeds? What one change can you make tonight to ensure you are among the successful on that day?

The Hadith of al-Nawwas on Jesus' Descent
Al-Buti quotes the hadith of al-Nawwas detailing Jesus' descent and battle with the Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of Jesus' descent from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, including his appearance, location, and his killing of the Dajjal.

Core Idea
Jesus descends at the white minaret east of Damascus and kills the Dajjal at Lod.

Al-Buti presents a lengthy hadith narrated by al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an that describes the Dajjal's appearance and the subsequent descent of Jesus. This hadith is one of the primary textual proofs for the physical descent of Jesus at the end of time.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith from al-Nawwas. Focus on the sequence of events.
2
Identify key details about Jesus
Note where Jesus descends, his description (hands on angel wings, dripping head), and the effect of his breath on disbelievers.
3
Trace the events after descent
Follow the narrative: Jesus pursues the Dajjal, kills him at the gate of Ludd, and then addresses the protected believers.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Jesus will descend at a specific location and kill the Dajjal with his very breath, how would that change your certainty about the unseen? Are you living as if the Hour could come at any moment, or do you let doubt creep in?
?
The hadith says no disbeliever who smells Jesus's breath dies. How does this vivid, physical description affect your conviction that these events are real? Do you struggle to accept the literal details, and if so, what does that reveal about your faith in the Prophet's report?
?
When the protected believers are told their ranks in Paradise, they receive immediate comfort. What rank are you striving for now? Are your daily actions deliberately preparing you for that moment, or are you hoping to be saved without effort?

The Consensus on Jesus' Descent: Hadith of Abu Huraira and Conclusion
Al-Buti provides a second hadith and concludes with tawatur and ijma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the additional proofs for Jesus' descent from the hadith of Abu Huraira and the basis for the Muslim consensus on this doctrine.

Core Idea
The descent of Jesus is confirmed by mutawatir hadith and the unanimous agreement of Muslims.

Al-Buti presents a second hadith from Abu Huraira that describes Jesus' actions after his descent, then argues that the hadith on this topic are mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and that the Muslim community has reached consensus (ijma') on the belief in his literal descent.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith of Abu Huraira
Read the hadith carefully. Note the description of Jesus' appearance and his actions after descent.
2
Understand the arguments for authenticity
Al-Buti lists multiple narrators and claims the hadith are mutawatir. He also cites Quranic verses (not quoted) as support.
3
Grasp the concept of consensus
Al-Buti concludes that because of these proofs, Muslims have unanimously accepted the belief in Jesus' descent. Reflect on the role of ijma' in Islamic doctrine.

الدخان، والدجال، والدابة، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها، ونزول عيسى بن مريم، ويأجوج ومأجوج، وثلاثة خسوف: خسف بالمشرق، وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم. ٣ - ما رويناه آنفاً عن مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي وأحمد وابن ماجه من حديث النواس بن سمعان رضي الله عنه عن رسول الله، بشأن الدجال، وفيه: فبينما هو كذلك إذ بعث الله المسيح بن مريم، فينزل عند المنارة البيضاء شرقي دمشق بين مهرودتين واضعاً كفيه على أجنحة ملكين، إذا طأطأ رأسه قطر، وإذا رفعه تحدر منه جمان كاللؤلؤ، فلا يحل لكافر يجد ريح نفسه إلا مات، ونفسه ينتهي حيث ينتهي طرفه فيطلبه حتى يدركه بباب لد فيقتله ثم يأتي عيسى قوم قد عصمهم الله منه، فيمسح عن وجوههم ويحدثهم بدرجاتهم في الجنة ... الحديث ٤ - ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود وابن جرير بطرق مختلفة عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله: «الأنبياء إخوة لعلات، أمهاتهم شتى ودينهم واحد، صلى الله عليه وسلم وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه، رجل مربوع، إلى الحمرة والبياض، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل: فيدق الصليب، ويقتل الخنزير، ويضع الجزية، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام، ويهلك المسيح الدجال، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله، من رواية أبي هريرة، وابن مسعود، وعثمان بن أبي العاص، وأبي أمامة، والنواس بن سمعان، وعبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
The Smoke, and the Dajjal, and the Beast, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus son of Mary, and Gog and Magog, and three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that comes out of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place. 3 - What we related previously from Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, Ahmad, and Ibn Majah from the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Messenger of Allah, concerning the Dajjal, and in it: 'While he is thus, Allah sends the Messiah son of Mary, and he descends at the white minaret east of Damascus, between two dyed garments, placing his hands on the wings of two angels; when he lowers his head, it drips, and when he raises it, drops fall from it like pearls; no disbeliever who smells his breath dies but he dies, and his breath reaches as far as his sight reaches; so he pursues him until he catches him at the gate of Ludd and kills him. Then Jesus comes to a people whom Allah has protected from him, and he wipes their faces and tells them of their ranks in Paradise... the hadith.' 4 - What Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Jarir narrated through various chains from Abu Hurayra, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The prophets are paternal brothers; their mothers are different but their religion is one. And I am the nearest of people to Jesus son of Mary because there was no prophet between me and him, and he will descend. When you see him, recognize him: a man of medium height, reddish-white, wearing two light-yellow garments, his head as if it is dripping though no moisture touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, impose the jizya, and call people to Islam. Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and he will destroy the Dajjal. Then he will remain on earth for forty years, then he will die, and the Muslims will pray over him.' So these are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary. There are many other hadiths which cannot be enumerated here. The summary is that they are hadiths of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Messenger of Allah, narrated by Abu Hurayra, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Usayd, may Allah be pleased with them all. And before that, we have examined the definitive verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same as these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have achieved consensus (ijma') on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His decisive declaration.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a continuous argument that begins with a classification of the major signs of the Hour, then focuses on the descent of Jesus as one of those signs, provides two detailed hadiths as proofs, and concludes with the affirmation of the doctrine based on tawatur and ijma'. The author first enumerates ten major events: the Smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three land sinkings (east, west, and Arabian Peninsula), and finally a fire from Yemen that drives people to their gathering place. This enumeration sets the eschatological context. Then he presents a lengthy hadith from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, which describes the Dajjal and Jesus' descent at the white minaret east of Damascus, his killing of the Dajjal at the gate of Ludd, and his care for the believers. The second hadith from Abu Hurayra emphasizes Jesus' role in breaking the cross, killing pigs, abolishing jizya, and calling to Islam, and states that he will remain on earth forty years. The author then asserts that these two hadiths, along with two others mentioned but not quoted, constitute a body of mutawatir (mass transmitted) reports, listing multiple companions as narrators. He further appeals to Quranic verses (unquoted) as supporting evidence and declares that the Muslims have reached consensus (ijma') on the literal bodily descent of Jesus at the end of time, confirming his bodily ascension. Thus, the passage establishes the doctrine through textual proof (hadith and Qur'an) and communal consensus, refuting any metaphorical interpretation.

Hadith and Consensus on the Descent of Jesus
Buti presents hadith evidence for Jesus's descent and states Muslim consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith evidence and Muslim consensus regarding the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The descent of Jesus is established by mutawatir hadith and unanimous consensus.

Buti presents the prophetic description of Jesus's return, then demonstrates that these hadith are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) and supported by Quranic verses, leading to the consensus of the entire Muslim community. This lesson explores how these sources together make the belief in Jesus's descent a definitive article of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith description
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the prophetic description of Jesus's appearance and actions come through.
Notice the vivid details: he breaks the cross, kills the pig, etc.
2
Note the claim of tawatur
Buti states that these hadith are mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and lists the Companions who narrated them. This elevates the level of certainty.
If hadith are mutawatir, they must be believed.
3
Understand how Quran and consensus reinforce
Buti mentions Quranic verses and then states that the entire Ummah has reached consensus (ijma') on this belief. This shows the doctrine is not based on hadith alone.
Consensus is a third source of certainty.

وإني أولى الناس بعيسى بن مريم لأنه لم يكن نبي بيني وبينه ، وإنه نازل فإذا رأيتموه فاعرفوه ، رجل مربوع ، إلى الحمرة والبياض ، عليه ثوبان ممصران كأن رأسه يقطر وإن لم يصبه بلل : فيدق الصليب ، ويقتل الخنزير ، ويضع الجزية ، ويدعو الناس إلى الإسلام ، ويهلك الله في زمانه الملل كلها إلا الإسلام ، ويهلك المسيح الدجال ، فيمكث في الأرض أربعين سنة ثم يتوفى ويصلي عليه المسلمون فهذه أربعة أحاديث تنص على نزول عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وهنالك أحاديث كثيرة أخرى لا مجال لسردها هنا ، والخلاصة أنها أحاديث متواترة عن رسول الله الله ، من رواية أبي هريرة ، وابن مسعود ، وعثمان بن أبي عليوة العاص ، وأبي أمامة ، والنواس بن سمعان ، وعبـد الله بن عمرو بن العاص ومجمع بن حارثة ، وحذيفة بن أسيد رضي الله عنهم ( وقد وقفت قبل ذلك على نصوص الآيات المحكمة من كتاب الله تعالى الناطقة بمثل ما دلت عليه هذه الأحاديث ؛ فمن أجل ذلك تم إجماع المسلمين على الاعتقاد بنزول عيسى ابن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمن ، على النحو وبالصفة التي ذكرها لنا رسول الله الله ، وأنه إنما رفع ببدنه حياً إلى السماء كما بين الله عز وجل صريحاً في محكم بيانه
And I am the most entitled of people to Jesus son of Mary, because there was no prophet between me and him. And indeed he is descending; so when you see him, recognize him: a man of medium stature, tending to redness and whiteness, wearing two garments lightly dyed with saffron, as if his head is dripping even though no wetness touches him. He will break the cross, kill the pig, abolish the jizya, and call people to Islam. And Allah will destroy in his time all religions except Islam, and will destroy the Dajjal. He will remain on earth forty years, then die, and the Muslims will pray over him. These are four hadiths that state the descent of Jesus son of Mary (peace and blessings be upon him), and there are many other hadiths for which there is no room to list here. The summary is that they are mutawatir hadiths from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), narrated by Abu Huraira, Ibn Mas'ud, Uthman ibn Abi al-As, Abu Umama, al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, Mujammi' ibn Haritha, and Hudhayfa ibn Asid (may Allah be pleased with them). And I have previously reviewed the clear verses from the Book of Allah Almighty that speak of the same thing that these hadiths indicate. Therefore, the Muslims have reached consensus on the belief in the descent of Jesus son of Mary (peace be upon him) at the end of time, in the manner and description that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) told us, and that he was raised bodily alive to heaven, as Allah Almighty clearly stated in His clear revelation.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents a composite hadith describing the descent of Jesus, then asserts that these (four) hadiths are mutawatir and are supported by Quranic verses, leading to the consensus of Muslims on the belief in Jesus's bodily ascension and future descent. Buti begins by quoting a well-known prophetic tradition that details Jesus's physical appearance and actions upon his return: he will break the cross, kill the pig, abolish the jizya, and call to Islam, and will remain on earth for forty years before dying a natural death and being buried by Muslims. Buti then states that this is one of four hadiths on the topic, and that there are many others which he does not list. He emphasizes that these hadiths are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), naming several Companions as narrators. He then mentions that Quranic verses also support this, and as a result, the entire Muslim ummah has reached consensus (ijma') on the belief that Jesus was raised bodily to heaven and will descend at the end of time exactly as the Prophet described. The passage thus establishes the doctrinal certainty of Jesus's nuzul (descent) through tawatur of hadith and ijma' of the community.

What is stopping you from starting today?

Refuting the Denial of Jesus' Descent and Critiquing Shaltut's Method
Refutes denial of Jesus' descent and criticizes Shaltut's method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the denial of Jesus' descent is a consequence of a broader rejection of miracles, and how scholars like Shaltut rely on weak arguments and a fringe school's approach.

Core Idea
Denial of Jesus' descent stems from a school that rejects miracles, not from Islamic evidence.

This passage critiques the method of Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut, who attempted to reinterpret Quranic verses and reject numerous authentic hadiths to deny the descent of Jesus (AS). The author argues that this denial is not an isolated opinion but a natural outgrowth of a school that undermines miracles while claiming to uphold Islam. By examining Shaltut's approach, we see the dangers of selective interpretation and reliance on a fringe group's authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify Shaltut's claims
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note Shaltut's argument about ahad hadith and his reinterpretation of verses.
Shaltut claims that the hadith on Jesus' descent are ahad and cannot form belief.
2
Understand the author's linking to the anti-miracle school
The author reminds you of a previous discussion about a school that denies miracles. See how he connects Shaltut's denial to that school as a 'natural echo.'
This is a key argument: the denial is not original but derivative.
3
Recognize the critique of Shaltut's method
The author points out the contradiction in trying to reconcile Islam with denial of miracles. He criticizes Shaltut for rejecting 70 hadiths and declaring all tafsir scholars wrong without evidence.
Notice the emphasis on lack of evidence for Shaltut's positions.
4
See the author's defense of the established understanding
The author mentions that he has provided hadith and Quranic verses that clearly support the descent. He ends by dismissing the fringe group's attempts to reinterpret the verse of raf'.
The conclusion is that their effort will not succeed.

أيـضاً قرب قيام الساعة . وقد كتب في ذلك الشيخ محمود شلتوت مقالاً في مجلة الرسالة » عدد ٤٦٢ أعقبه بكتابة مقالات أخرى في نفس المبحث ؛ وكان الذي انتهى إليه في مقالاته تلك ، هو تأويل الآيات الواردة ، والإعراض عن الأحاديث الكثيرة الثابتة، زاعماً أنها أحاديث آحاد لا يصلح أن يقام عليهـا الاعتقاد !! . ولعلك قد قرأت ما كتبناه عن موقف العلم والعقل من المعجزة في بحث النبوات ، ووقفت إذ ذاك على قصة المدرسة التي قامت تنكر المعجزة دون أن تنكر الدين صراحة ، كما وقفت على سر انبعاث تلك المدرسة والظروف المكونة لها . فإذا ذكرت ما قد قلناه إذ ذاك ، فاعلم أن إنكار نزول عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام على الرغم مما ثبت في ذلك من الأدلة القاطعة ، ليس إلا صدى طبيعياً من أصداء تلك المدرسة وثمرة تتفق كل الاتفاق مع مبادئها . بيد أن كلاً من الاضطراب والتخبط الأعمى اللذين لا يبالي أن يقع فيهما دعاة تلك المدرسة وأتباعها ، يتمثل في محاولة التوفيق والجمع بين التمسك بالإسلام والتمسك بإنكار الخوارق والمعجزات !! ونحن لانشك في أنها محاولة من حيث الظاهر فحسب ، اتقاء لغضب المسلمين وتدرجاً في التسلل إلى موضع العقيدة من قلوبهم . فهذا التخبط في محاولة التوفيق ، هو الذي جعل واحداً مثل الشيخ شلتوت لا يبالي أن يكذِّب سبعين حديثاً مع رواتها ، وأن يخطئ عامة المفسرين لكتاب الله منذ عصر الصحابة إلى بزوغ مدرسة أستاذه - في سبيل أن تسلم له عقيدة إنكار الخوارق والمعجزات !! والأعجب من ذلك أن يكذب الأحاديث بدون شاهد ، أو صورة شاهد على الكذب ... وأن يخطئ المفسرين بدون شاهد ، أو صورة شاهد على الخطأ !. نعم ثمة شاهد واحد ، هو شذوذ تلك الشرذمة التي قامت لأسباب ودوافع معروفة ، تنكر الخوارق والمعجزات. فهذا هو الشاهد الذي يسوع امتلاخ نصوص السنة ودلالات الكتاب من جذورها والإعراض عنها جملة وتفصيلاً !! أما السنة فقد نقلنا لك بعضاً يسيراً منها ، وقد وقفت على دلالتها الصريحة التي لا تقبل أي قال وقيل حولها . وأما الكتاب فقد نقلنا لك من آياته آيتين كل منها ذو دلالة واضحة على المعنى الذي أخذ به عامة المفسرين ، والصحابة الكرام غير أن هذه الشرذمة تركز كل اهتمامها على تأويل آية الرفع وجرها إلى معنى الرفع بالروح أو رفع الدرجة ، تصوراً منها بأن طلاء التأويل إذا تماسك على نصوص الرفع ، فإنه يتماسك بعد ذلك بكل سهولة على نصوص النزول . وهيهات أن يتم لهم ذلك
Also, the nearness of the Hour. Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut wrote an article in Al-Risala magazine issue 462, followed by other articles on the same topic; and what he concluded in those articles was the interpretation of the verses and the disregard of the many authentic hadiths, claiming that they are singular (ahad) hadiths that cannot be relied upon for belief!! And perhaps you have read what we wrote about the position of science and reason regarding miracles in the discussion of prophethood, and you came to know the story of the school that denied miracles without explicitly denying religion, as you came to know the secret of the emergence of that school and the circumstances that formed it. So if you recall what we said then, know that the denial of the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) despite the conclusive evidence established on that, is nothing but a natural echo of that school and a fruit that fully agrees with its principles. However, both the confusion and blind floundering that the proponents of that school and their followers do not care to fall into, are manifested in the attempt to reconcile and combine adherence to Islam and adherence to the denial of supernatural events (khawariq) and miracles!! We have no doubt that it is an attempt only in appearance, fearing the anger of Muslims and gradually infiltrating into the place of faith in their hearts. This floundering in the attempt to reconcile is what made someone like Sheikh Shaltut not care to deny seventy hadiths with their narrators, and to consider the majority of commentators of the Book of God wrong from the time of the Companions to the emergence of his teacher's school - so that his doctrine of denial of miracles and supernatural events could be preserved!! And more astonishing than that is that he denies the hadiths without evidence, or the semblance of evidence, for their denial... And he declares the commentators wrong without evidence, or the semblance of evidence for their error. Yes, there is one evidence: the deviance of that fringe group that arose for known reasons and motives, denying miracles and supernatural events. This is the evidence that justifies uprooting the texts of the Sunnah and the indications of the Book from their roots and disregarding them entirely and in detail!! As for the Sunnah, we have transmitted to you a small part of it, and you have seen its explicit indication that does not accept any 'he said' and 'they said' around it. As for the Book, we have transmitted to you two verses, each of which has a clear indication of the meaning that the majority of commentators and the noble Companions adopted, except that this fringe group focuses all its attention on interpreting the verse of the raising (raf') and pulling it to the meaning of raising in spirit or raising in rank, imagining that if the paint of interpretation coheres on the texts of raising, then it will cohere afterwards with all ease on the texts of descent. Far be it from them to achieve that.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the denial of the descent of Jesus (AS) and a critique of the method of Sheikh Mahmoud Shaltut and his school. The author begins by referencing Shaltut's articles where he interpreted verses and rejected many authentic hadiths, claiming they are ahad (solitary) and not suitable for belief. The author then reminds the reader of previous discussions about the school that denied miracles while not explicitly denying religion. He states that the denial of Jesus' descent is a natural consequence of that school. He points out the contradiction in attempting to reconcile Islam with denial of miracles, calling it a mere facade to avoid Muslim anger. He then criticizes Shaltut for rejecting seventy hadiths without evidence and declaring all tafsir scholars wrong, relying only on the deviance of a fringe group. Finally, he mentions that he has provided some hadith and two verses from the Quran that clearly support the meaning held by the majority of commentators and Companions, but the fringe group focuses on interpreting the verse of the raising (raf') to avoid the meaning of descent. The author concludes that their attempt will not succeed.

Linguistic Refutation of 'Tawaffi' as Death in Jesus Verse
Linguistically refutes claiming 'mutawaffika' means death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Arabic word 'tawaffi' literally means 'to take completely' and that its use for death is metaphorical, thus refuting the claim that the verse indicates Jesus died.

Core Idea
'Tawaffi' does not mean death; it means taking completely.

This lesson examines a key linguistic argument used to refute the claim that Jesus died. The verse 'Inni mutawaffika' is often misunderstood by those who take 'tawaffi' as synonymous with 'death'. The author clarifies the true meaning of the word and shows that death is only one metaphorical application.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and the claim
Read the verse from Ali Imran 55 and the claim that 'mutawaffika' means 'causing your death'.
2
Understand the linguistic refutation
The author argues that 'tawaffi' means taking something completely, not necessarily death. Note the example 'istawfaytu haqqi'.
The root w-f-y means to complete.
3
See why the misconception arose
Common people use 'tawaffi' only for death, but its original meaning is broader. Scholars like al-Zamakhshari confirm that using it for death is metaphorical.
This is a key point: metaphorical usage does not cancel the literal meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأكثر ما يتعلقون به ، في هذا الصدد ، كلمة « متوفيك « من قوله تعالى : إذ قال اللهُ يَاعيسَى إِنِّي مُتَوَفِّيكَ وَرافِعُكَ إِلَيَّ ومُطَهِّرُكَ مِنَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا * [ آل عمران : ٥٥ ] ظناً بأن متوفيك مرادفة لميتك ! ولم يقل أحد من علماء اللغة ذلك ، بل التوفي معناه أخذ الشيء وقبضه تماماً ، ومرادفه الاستيفاء . نقول : استوفيت حقي وتوفيته أي قبضته كاملاً . أما الإماتة التي هي أخذ الروح، فهي نوع من أنواع التوفي الذي يشملها وغيرها وإنما سرى الوهم إلى هؤلاء من كثرة استعمال عامة الناس هذه الكلمة بمعنى الموت فقط وغفلة عن معناها الأصلي في اللغة . ولو رجع هؤلاء إلى اللغة لرأوا أن التعبير بالتوفي عن الموت يأتي في الدرجة الدلالة اللغوية ، كما يقول العلامة مصطفى صبري . ولذلك نص الزمخشري في كتابه أساس البلاغة على أن التعبير بالوفاة عن الموت من المجاز .
And what they cling to most, in this regard, is the word 'mutawaffika' from His statement: 'When Allah said, O Jesus, I will take you (mutawaffika) and raise you to Me and purify you from those who disbelieve.' (Ali Imran 55) supposing that 'mutawaffika' is synonymous with 'mumituka' (causing your death)! But none of the linguists have said that. Rather, 'tawaffi' means taking something and seizing it completely, and its synonym is 'istifa' (receiving in full). We say: 'istawfaytu haqqi wa tawaffaytuhu' meaning I received it completely. As for causing death (imata), which is the taking of the soul, it is a type of 'tawaffi' that includes it and others. The illusion only entered into them from the frequent use of this word by common people only in the sense of death, and heedlessness of its original meaning in the language. If they had referred to the language, they would have seen that the expression of 'tawaffi' for death comes in the second degree of linguistic signification, as the scholar Mustafa Sabri says. Therefore, al-Zamakhshari stated in his book Asas al-Balagha that the expression of 'wafat' for death is metaphorical.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic refutation of the misinterpretation of the word 'mutawaffika' in the verse. The author states that the deniers cling to this word thinking it means 'causing death'. He refutes this by explaining that linguistically, 'tawaffi' means to take something completely, not necessarily death. He gives the example of 'istawfaytu haqqi' (I received my right fully). He explains that death (imata) is only one type of tawaffi, as it is the taking of the soul. The confusion arose because common people use the word mainly for death. The author cites the scholar Mustafa Sabri and al-Zamakhshari to show that the use of 'tawaffi' for death is metaphorical, not literal. Therefore, the verse does not prove that Jesus died; rather, it means Allah took him up entirely.

Linguistic Proof that Jesus Was Physically Raised to Heaven
The author uses Arabic grammar to prove the literal meaning of the ascension verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Arabic particle 'bal' in Quran 4:158 necessitates a literal physical raising of Jesus to heaven, and why metaphorical interpretations are linguistically invalid.

Core Idea
The particle 'bal' demands a real negation and opposite, not a mere shift in meaning.

This lesson examines a key Quranic verse (4:157-158) that describes Jesus' fate. Using Arabic grammar, the author demonstrates that the word 'bal' (rather) forces a literal interpretation: if the Jews did not kill Jesus, then Allah must have physically raised him. This linguistic argument refutes metaphorical interpretations that claim only his rank was raised.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse
Start by reading verses 4:157-158 in Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: a negation ('they did not kill him') followed by 'bal' then a positive statement.
The verse is the foundation of the argument.
2
Understand the function of 'bal'
The author gives three examples showing that 'bal' must cancel the preceding clause and assert a contrary reality. Reflect on why 'I am not hungry, but I am lying down' is incorrect while 'I am not hungry, but I am full' is correct.
The key is that 'bal' requires a direct opposite.
3
Apply the rule to the verse
Apply the logic of 'bal' to 'They did not kill him, but Allah raised him to Himself.' The opposite of killing is not raising rank but physical preservation. Conclude that the raising must be literal.
The contrast must be real: physical death vs. physical ascension.
4
Examine Sheikh Shaltut's interpretation
Consider the author's refutation of Shaltut's claim that the raising is of rank. The author poses rhetorical questions: what does 'to Him' mean? Why restrict it to the crucifixion context?
These questions show the metaphorical reading is inconsistent.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
The author concludes that denying miracles leads to flawed interpretation. Consider how linguistic rules protect correct theological understanding.
This highlights the importance of sound methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي ينفي احتمال المجاز في (متوفيك) في هذه الآية، دلالة الآية القاطعة الأخرى التي لا مجال للتأويل فيها:
يقول الله عز وجل في سورة النساء: 157 و158: ﴿ وَقَولِهِمْ إِنَّا قَتَلْنَا الْمَسِيحَ عِيسَى ابْنَ مَرْيَمَ رَسُولَ اللهِ وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ وَمَا صَلَبُوهُ وَلَٰكِن شُبِّهَ لَهُمْ وَإِنَّ الَّذِينَ اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ لَفِي شَكٍّ مِّنْهُ مَا لَهُم بِهِ مِنْ عِلْمٍ إِلَّا اتِّبَاعَ الظَّنِّ وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ يَقِينًا بَل رَّفَعَهُ اللهُ إِلَيْهِ وَكَانَ اللهُ عَزِيزًا حَكِيمًا ﴾
فأما عقل العاقل الذي يفهم الكلام العربي عن طريق قواعد اللغة العربية ودلالاتها اللغوية، فهو يفهم من قوله تعالى: (وَمَا قَتَلُوهُ يَقِينًا بَل رَّفَعَهُ اللهُ إِلَيْهِ) أن الله عز وجل أخفى نبيه عنهم بأن رفعه إلى سمائه فلم يقعوا منه على شيء يقتلونه أو يصلبونه. يدلك على هذا المعنى ألفاظ الآية ودلالاتها اللغوية وضرورة التقابل الذي ينبغي أن يكون بين ما قبل بل وما بعدها. فليس لك أن تقول، وأنت عربي: لست جائعاً بل أنا مضطجع، وإنما تقول: لست جائعاً بل أنا شبعان. وليس لك أن تقول: ما مات خالد بل هو رجل صالح، وإنما تقول: بل هو حي. وليس لك أن تقول: ما قتل الأمير بل هو ذو درجة عالية عند الله، لأن كونه ذو درجة عالية عند الله لا ينافي أن يقتل، وإنما تأتي بل لإبطال ما قبلها بدليل مما بعدها.
لا جرم إذاً أن معنى الآية: ما قتله اليهود كما زعموا بل إن الله استلبه من بينهم ورفعه إلى السماء، ولكن الشيخ شلتوت يأبى إلا أن يكون المعنى: ما قتلوه، بل رفع الله درجته إليه، وذلك على الرغم من أنف القواعد العربية ودلالاتها وعلى الرغم من أنف العرب والمفسرين كلهم.
ولك أن تسأل أمثال الشيخ شلتوت، وهم يذهبون في تفسير الآية هذا المذهب: فما معنى «إليه» في الآية مادام أن الرفع هو رفع الدرجة؟ هل المعنى أن الله جعله إلها مثله؟!
إذ لا معنى لقولك: إن الله رفع مقام فلان إليه، إلا أنه قد جعله في مرتبته؟!
ثم ما معنى تقييد رفع الدرجة بحال قصد الصلب أو القتل؟ أو لم يكن مرفوع الدرجة قبل ذلك؟!
أسئلة لا جواب عليها، إلا استجرار الكلام والتأويل التي لا معنى لها، خدمة لما استقر في نفوسهم من مرض إنكار الخوارق والمعجزات ورحم الله من أبدع المثل القائل: بأن رجلاً نظر إلى حمار يافع فاشتهى لحمه، فالتفت إلى من حوله قائلاً: ما أشبه أذنيه بأذني الأرنب!
And that which negates the possibility of metaphor in 'mutawaffīka' in this verse is the indication of the other decisive verse which allows no interpretation: Allah Almighty says in Surah an-Nisa, 157-158: "And their saying, 'Indeed, we have killed the Messiah, Jesus, the son of Mary, the messenger of Allah.' And they did not kill him, nor did they crucify him; but [rather] it was made to appear to them. And indeed, those who differ over it are in doubt about it. They have no knowledge of it except the following of assumption. And they did not kill him, for certain. Rather, Allah raised him to Himself. And ever is Allah Exalted in Might and Wise." As for the mind of the intelligent person who understands Arabic speech through the rules of the Arabic language and its linguistic indications, he understands from His saying: "And they did not kill him, for certain. Rather, Allah raised him to Himself" that Allah Almighty concealed His prophet from them by raising him to His heaven, so they did not obtain from him anything to kill or crucify. This meaning is indicated to you by the words of the verse and its linguistic indications and the necessity of the contrast that must exist between what precedes 'bal' and what follows it. For you cannot say, while being Arab: 'I am not hungry, but rather I am lying down.' Rather, you say: 'I am not hungry, but rather I am full.' And you cannot say: 'Khalid did not die, but rather he is a righteous man.' Rather, you say: 'Rather, he is alive.' And you cannot say: 'The prince was not killed, but rather he has a high rank with Allah,' because his being of high rank with Allah does not negate that he was killed. Rather, 'bal' comes to invalidate what precedes it by evidence from what follows it. Therefore, inevitably, the meaning of the verse is: The Jews did not kill him as they claimed, but rather Allah snatched him from among them and raised him to heaven. But Sheikh Shaltut insists that the meaning be: They did not kill him, but rather Allah raised his rank to Him, this despite the nose of the Arabic rules and their indications and despite the nose of the Arabs and all the commentators. And you may ask the likes of Sheikh Shaltut, while they go in interpreting the verse this way: So what is the meaning of 'ilayhi' (to Him) in the verse, since the raising is the raising of rank? Does it mean that Allah made him a god like Him?! For there is no meaning to your saying: 'Allah raised the rank of so-and-so to Him,' unless He made him in His rank?! Then what is the meaning of restricting the raising of rank to the situation of intending crucifixion or killing? Was he not of high rank before that?! Questions that have no answer, except dragging speech and interpretation which have no meaning, serving the illness that has settled in their hearts of denying miracles and marvels. And may Allah have mercy on the one who invented the saying: A man looked at a young donkey and desired its meat, so he turned to those around him saying: 'How similar are its ears to the ears of a rabbit!'
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage presents a linguistic argument defending the literal interpretation of the Quranic verse about Jesus being raised to heaven. The author begins by citing the Quranic verses 4:157-158, then explains how an Arabic speaker would understand the function of the particle 'bal' (بل). He gives three examples showing that 'bal' must negate the preceding clause and affirm the opposite: e.g., 'I am not hungry, but rather I am full' (contrast: lying down would be illogical). He applies this to the verse: the Jews did not kill Jesus; rather, Allah raised him to Himself. He then refutes Sheikh Shaltut's claim that the raising is merely of rank, using rhetorical questions: if the raising is of rank, what does 'to Him' mean? And why would it be restricted to the context of the crucifixion attempt? He concludes that such interpretations stem from a psychological denial of miracles and dismisses them with a satirical analogy about a man who sees a donkey and compares its ears to a rabbit's.

مُتَوَفِّيك
رفع
تأويل
مجاز
شلتوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the particle 'bal' can be used simply to contrast without fully negating the previous statement.
Correction: The author shows that 'bal' demands complete negation and the establishment of a direct opposite, as demonstrated by the examples.

Checkpoint
What linguistic function does the author attribute to 'بل' (bal) in the verse?
A) It indicates a mere addition.
B) It invalidates what precedes and establishes the opposite.
C) It provides a reason for the preceding.
D) It marks a change of topic.

Key Takeaway
The Arabic particle 'bal' forces a literal reading of Jesus' ascension as a physical event, and denying this leads to linguistically and theologically unsound interpretations.

The Emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj: A Major Sign of the Hour
Buti explains the Quranic account of Ya'juj and Ma'juj and their appearance before the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic account of Ya'juj and Ma'juj, their nature as a major sign of the Hour, and that the timing of their appearance is known only to Allah.

Core Idea
Ya'juj and Ma'juj are a great nation whose sudden emergence is a major sign of the approaching Hour, but only Allah knows when.

In this lesson, we explore the Quranic description of Ya'juj and Ma'juj (Gog and Magog). Buti explains that these terms refer to a vast, destructive nation that will appear suddenly as one of the major signs of the Hour. The Quran conceals the timing, but affirms their emergence as a portent of the end. We will examine the Quranic verses that describe their release and the barrier built by Dhul-Qarnayn.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of Buti's explanation.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses quoted.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice the three main points: the definition of Ya'juj and Ma'juj, the concealment of their timing, and their role as a major sign of the Hour.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Consider how the verses from Surah Al-Anbiya' and Al-Kahf support Buti's explanation. What do they say about the emergence and the barrier?
The verses describe both the release and the eventual destruction of the barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳ - ظهور يأجوج ومأجوج : يأجوج ومأجوج : هاتان الكلمتان عبر بها القرآن عن أمة كبيرة من الناس يفاجأ بها العالم تنسل إليه من كل حدب، تنشر الفساد والدمار في الأرض، على نحو مذهل وبطريقة مرعبة. غير أن القرآن أخفى عن الناس ميعاد ظهورهم. فلا يعلم أجل ذلك أحد إلا الله عز وجل. ولكنه نص على أن ظهورهم علامة من العلامات الكبرى لاقتراب الساعة. وهذا هو إخبار القرآن عنهم: حتى إذا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُم مِن كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنسِلُونَ * وَاقتَرَبَ الوَعدُ الحَقُّ فَإِذَا هِيَ شَاخِصَةٌ أَبْصَارُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يَا وَيلَنَا قَد كُنَّا فِي غَفلَةٍ مِن هَذَا بَل كُنَّا ظَالِمِينَ [الأنبياء: ٩٦-٩٧]. قالُوا يَا ذَا القَرنَينِ إِنَّ يَأجُوجَ وَمَأجُوجَ مُفسِدُونَ فِي الأَرضِ فَهَل نَجعَلُ لَكَ خَرجًا عَلَى أَن تَجعَلَ بَينَنَا وَبَينَهُم سَدًّا * قَالَ مَا مَكَّنِي فِيهِ رَبِّي خَيرٌ فَأَعِينُونِي بِقُوَّةٍ أَجعَل بَينَكُم وَبَينَهُم رَدْمًا * آتُونِي زُبَرَ الحَدِيدِ حَتَّى إِذَا سَاوَى بَينَ الصَّدَفَينِ قَالَ انفُخُوا حَتَّى إِذَا جَعَلَهُ نَارًا قَالَ آتُونِي أُفرِغ عَلَيهِ قِطرًا * فَمَا اسطَاعُوا أَن يَظهَرُوهُ وَمَا استَطَاعُوا لَهُ نَقبًا * قَالَ هَذَا رَحمَةٌ مِن رَبِّي فَإِذَا جَاءَ وَعدُ رَبِّي جَعَلَهُ دَكَّاءَ وَكَانَ وَعدُ رَبِّي حَقًّا * وَتَرَكنَا بَعضَهُم يَومَئِذٍ يَمُوجُ فِي بَعضٍ [الكهف: ٩٤-٩٩]. أما أخبار السنة عنهم، فتأكيد للذي أخبر عنهم القرآن.
3 - The emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj: Ya'juj and Ma'juj: these two words the Quran uses to describe a great nation of people with which the world will be suddenly confronted, slipping out from every hill, spreading corruption and destruction on the earth, in an astounding manner and a terrifying way. However, the Quran concealed from people the appointed time of their emergence. So no one knows its term except Allah Almighty. But He stated that their emergence is a major sign of the approach of the Hour. And this is the Quran's report about them: "Until when Ya'juj and Ma'juj are let loose and they swoop down from every hill. And the true promise draws near; then behold, the eyes of those who disbelieved stare fixedly: 'Woe to us! We were indeed heedless of this; nay, we were wrongdoers.'" [Al-Anbiya': 96-97]. They said: "O Dhul-Qarnayn, indeed Ya'juj and Ma'juj are corrupting on the earth; so may we assign to you a tribute that you may make a barrier between us and them?" He said: "That wherein my Lord has established me is better; so assist me with strength; I will make between you and them a rampart. Bring me blocks of iron." Until when he had leveled between the two cliffs, he said: "Blow," until when he had made it fire, he said: "Bring me, that I may pour over it molten copper." So they were not able to scale it, nor were they able to pierce it. He said: "This is a mercy from my Lord; but when the promise of my Lord comes, He will level it to the ground; and the promise of my Lord is ever true." And on that Day, We will leave them surging like waves over one another [Al-Kahf: 94-99]. As for the reports of the Sunnah about them, they are a confirmation of what the Quran reported about them.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a Quranic lesson about Ya'juj and Ma'juj (Gog and Magog). Buti begins by defining the term, stating that the Quran uses these words to refer to a great nation of people whose sudden emergence from every direction will cause widespread corruption and destruction in a stunning and terrifying manner. He then notes that the exact time of their appearance is hidden by the Quran; only Allah knows it. However, the Quran explicitly states that their emergence is one of the major signs of the approaching Hour. To support this, Buti quotes two sets of Quranic verses. First, from Surah Al-Anbiya' (21:96-97), which describes the release of Ya'juj and Ma'juj and the reaction of the disbelievers when the true promise (the Hour) approaches. Second, from Surah Al-Kahf (18:94-99), which recounts the story of Dhul-Qarnayn and the building of a barrier against Ya'juj and Ma'juj, but also indicates that this barrier will be destroyed when the promise of the Lord comes, leading to chaos. Finally, Buti mentions that the hadith reports about them simply confirm what the Quran has already stated.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
العلامات الكبرى
الساعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ya'juj and Ma'juj have already appeared or are a specific historical tribe.
Correction: The Quran describes their emergence as a future major sign of the Hour, not a past event.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what does the Quran say about the timing of the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj?
A) It is known to the scholars
B) It is concealed and known only to Allah
C) It will be announced by the Prophet
D) It occurs regularly throughout history

Key Takeaway
Ya'juj and Ma'juj are a great nation whose sudden, destructive emergence is a major sign of the Hour, but their exact time of appearance is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj is a sign of the Hour, your heart may feel distant from that reality. But if you are honest with yourself, do you live today as if the Hour could come at any moment, or do you behave like the heedless disbelievers who will say 'We were heedless of this'? What one concrete change will you make this week to prepare for that Day?
?
The barrier of Dhul-Qarnayn was a mercy from Allah, yet it was ultimately temporary and will be destroyed. What barriers have you built in your life to protect yourself from sin—your routines, your environment, your self-discipline? Are you relying on those barriers or on the One who controls their destruction? How can you shift your trust from your own efforts to Allah's promise that His decree will come?
?
The exact time of Ya'juj and Ma'juj is known only to Allah. If He were to unveil to you that the Hour would begin one month from today, what would you do differently? Why are you not doing that now? Do not let yourself ignore the urgency of this lesson—write down one action you will start doing today as if the signs are already unfolding.

Yajuj and Majuj: Definition and Quranic Evidence
Defines Yajuj and Majuj and quotes Quranic verses about them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic definition of Yajuj and Majuj as a real nation whose emergence is a major sign of the Hour, supported by two Quranic passages.

Core Idea
Yajuj and Majuj are a literal nation whose sudden release marks the approach of the Hour.

This lesson introduces Yajuj and Majuj, a people mentioned in the Quran. The author defines them as a vast nation that will cause widespread destruction. He also presents two key Quranic passages that describe their emergence and the barrier built by Dhul-Qarnayn. Let's read the source passage and explore its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author combines definition with direct Quranic quotation.
2
Identify the definition of Yajuj and Majuj
Find how the author defines Yajuj and Majuj: they are a great nation that will suddenly emerge, spreading corruption. Note that their time is unknown but their appearance is a major sign.
The definition is in the first few lines before the verses.
3
Study the first Quranic passage
Read Al-Anbiya' 96-97. Notice how it describes their release and the reaction of the disbelievers. The verse emphasizes the suddenness and terror of the event.
This passage highlights the eschatological significance.
4
Study the second Quranic passage
Read Al-Kahf 94-99. This passage narrates the story of Dhul-Qarnayn building a barrier against Yajuj and Majuj, which will be levelled at the appointed time.
This shows that their containment is temporary and that their release is decreed by Allah.
5
Reflect on the significance as a major sign
Connect these passages to the broader topic of the major signs of the Hour. Consider why the author emphasizes that the time of appearance is hidden but the fact of appearance is certain.
This reinforces the Quranic teaching on the unseen.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يأجوج ومأجوج : هاتان الكلمتان عبر بها القرآن عن أمة كبيرة من الناس يفاجأ بها العالم تنسل إليه من كل حدب ، تنشر الفساد والدمار في الأرض ، على نحو مذهل وبطريقة مرعبة . غير أن القرآن أخفى عن الناس ميعاد ظهورهم . فلا يعلم أجل ذلك أحد إلا الله عز وجل . ولكنه نص على أن ظهورهم علامة من العلامات الكبرى لاقتراب الساعة . وهذا هو إخبار القرآن عنهم : حتى إذا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُم مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ واقتَرَبَ الوَعدُ الحَقُّ فَإذا هِيَ شاخِصَةٌ أَبْصَارُ الَّذِينَ كَفَروا ، يَا وَيْلَنَا قَدْ كُنَّا فِي غَفْلَةٍ مِن هذا بَل كُنَّا ظالمين ) [ الأنبياء : ٩٦ - ٩٧ ] . ل .. قالُوا يَا ذَا القَرْنَيْنِ إِنْ يَأْجُوجَ وَمَأْجُوجَ مُفْسِدُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ ، فَهَل نَجْعَلُ لَكَ خَرْجاً على أن تَجْعَلَ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَهُم سَداً قال ما مكني فِيهِ رَبِّي خَيْرٌ ، فأعينُونِي بقوَّةٍ أَجْعَلْ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَهُمْ رَدماً . آتُونِي زُبَرِ الحَديدِ حَتَّى إذا ساوى بينَ الصَّدَفَيْنِ قال انفُخُوا حَتَّى إذا جَعَلَهُ ناراً قَالَ أَتُونِي أُفْرِغْ عَلَيْهِ قطراً . فا اسطاعُوا أن يَظْهَرُوهُ وَما استطاعُوا لَهُ نَقْباً قالَ هَذا رَحْمَةٌ مِنْ رَبِّي فَإِذَا جَاءَ وَعدُ رَبِّي جَعَلَهُ دَكّاءَ وَكان وعد ربي حقاً
Yajuj and Majuj: these two words, the Qur'an used to refer to a great nation of people that the world will suddenly be surprised by, emerging from every elevated place, spreading corruption and destruction on the earth, in a staggering manner and terrifying way. But the Qur'an concealed from people the time of their appearance. No one knows its appointed time except Allah Almighty. Rather, it stated that their appearance is one of the major signs of the approach of the Hour. This is the Qur'an's report about them: "Until when Gog and Magog are let loose and they race down from every elevated place. And the true promise has drawn near; then behold, the eyes of those who disbelieved will be staring in horror, [saying], 'Woe to us! We were indeed heedless of this; rather, we were wrongdoers.'" [Al-Anbiya': 96-97]. They said, "O Dhul-Qarnayn, indeed Gog and Magog are corrupting the earth; so may we assign for you an expenditure that you might make between us and them a barrier?" He said, "That in which my Lord has established me is better; but assist me with strength; I will make between you and them a fortification. Bring me sheets of iron until, when he had leveled [them] between the two mountain sides, he said, 'Blow [with bellows],' until when he had made it fire, he said, 'Bring me molten copper to pour over it.' So they were not able to scale it, nor were they able to penetrate it. He said, 'This is a mercy from my Lord; but when the promise of my Lord comes, He will make it level, and ever is the promise of my Lord true.'" [Al-Kahf: 94-99]

Commentary
This passage defines Yajuj and Majuj and presents the Quranic evidence. The author begins by explaining that 'Yajuj and Majuj' are Quranic terms for a vast nation whose sudden emergence will bring destruction. The time of their appearance is unknown, but their emergence is a major sign of the approaching Hour. The author then quotes two Quranic passages. The first (Al-Anbiya' 96-97) describes their release and the reaction of the disbelievers. The second (Al-Kahf 94-99) narrates the story of Dhul-Qarnayn building a barrier against them, which will be levelled when the promise of the Lord comes. The interpretation follows the apparent meaning: Yajuj and Majuj are real people, and their escapement is a future event. The author does not comment on allegorical interpretations.

Hadith Evidence on Yajuj and Majuj as a Major Sign
Presents three hadiths confirming Yajuj and Majuj and emphasizes the limits of creedal certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key hadith evidence establishing Yajuj and Majuj as a major sign of the Hour and the principle that only certain details are creedally binding.

Core Idea
The Qur'an and authentic hadiths confirm Yajuj and Majuj's emergence; most details come from weak sources.

This lesson presents three authentic hadiths that confirm what the Qur'an states about Gog and Magog. These reports are foundational for Muslim belief in this major sign. At the same time, the lesson draws an important boundary: while the general fact of their emergence is certain, many circulating details are unreliable and not part of creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths with attention
Read the three hadiths: the one from Zaynab bint Jahsh, the long hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an (excerpt), and the list of ten signs from Hudhayfa ibn Asid. Note the key elements each adds.
The first shows the Prophet's alarm, the second describes their effect on Lake Tiberias, the third lists them among ten major signs.
2
Understand the author's conclusion
The author states that these hadiths provide conclusive evidence (dalala qati'a) that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of the Hour. Belief in this is necessary for faith in the Book and Sunnah.
3
Distinguish between certain and speculative
The author warns that most details about their attributes, physical forms, and specific reports come from weak or fabricated hadiths. In matters of creed, we must not rely on such sources.
This is a key principle: only what is authentically established is binding in 'aqida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما أخبار السنة عنهم ، فتأكيد للذي أخبر عنهم القرآن . روى الشيخان وغيرهما عن زينب بنت جحش أن النبي استيقظ من نومه وهو يقول : لا إله إلا الله ، ويل للعرب من شر قد اقترب ، فتح اليوم من ردم يأجوج ومأجوج مثل هذه . وعقد الراوي بيده عشرة . قلت : يارسول الله أنهلك وفينا الصالحون ؟ قال : نعم إذا كثر الخبث . وروى مسلم والترمذي وابن ماجه وأحمد عن النواس بن سمعان الحديث الطويل الذي ذكرناه آنفاً والذي فيه خبر الدجال وعيسى بن مريم ، وفيه : « ويبعث يأجوج ومأجوج وهم من كل حدب ينسلون فيمر أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية فيشربون ما فيها ، ويمر آخر هم فيقولون : لقد كان بهذه مرة ماء . وروى مسلم وأبو داود والترمذي وابن ماجه عن حذيفة بن أسيد الغفاري عنه ، قال : طلع علينا النبي ونحن نتذاكر ، فقال : مــا تذاكرون ؟ قالوا : نذكر الساعة ، قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آیات : الدخان ، والدجال ، والدابة ، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ، ونزول عيسى بن مريم ، ويأجوج ومأجوج ، وثلاث خسوف : خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب وخسف بجزيرة العرب ، وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من أرض اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم . فتلك الآيات وهذه الأحاديث ، ذات دلالة قاطعة على أن من أشراط الساعة ظهور هذه الأمة التي تعثو فساداً في الأرض . فكان الإيمان بذلك من الضروريات التي لابد منها للإيمان بالكتاب والسنة . أما علم ما وراء ذلك من التفصيلات المتعلقة بصفاتهم وكيفياتهم ، وتفصيل أخبارهم معظم ما ورد من تفاصيل أخبارهم وصفاتهم وأشكال جسومهم ، إنما تناقله الناس عن طريق أحاديث واهية أو منكرة أو باطلة ، فلا مطمع في باب العقيدة في الوصول إلى شيء من ذلك .
As for the reports of the Sunnah about them, they are confirmation of what the Qur'an reported about them. Al-Bukhari and Muslim and others narrated from Zaynab bint Jahsh that the Prophet woke up from his sleep saying: 'There is no god but Allah, woe to the Arabs from an evil that has drawn near. Today a gap has been opened in the barrier of Gog and Magog like this.' And the narrator clasped his hand to indicate ten. I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, will we be destroyed while there are righteous among us?' He said: 'Yes, when wickedness increases.' And Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, and Ahmad narrated from al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an the long hadith we mentioned earlier which includes the story of the Dajjal and Jesus son of Mary, and in it: 'Gog and Magog will be sent forth and they will race down from every elevated place, and their first ones will pass by Lake Tiberias and drink what is in it, and their last ones will pass and say: There was once water here.' And Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah narrated from Hudhayfa ibn Asid al-Ghifari, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Prophet came upon us while we were discussing. He said: 'What are you discussing?' We said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not come until you see before it ten signs: the smoke, the Dajjal, the beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, three landslides: a landslide in the east, a landslide in the west, and a landslide in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that will emerge from the land of Yemen driving the people to their gathering place.' So these verses and these hadiths are conclusive evidence that among the signs of the Hour is the appearance of this nation that spreads corruption in the earth. Thus belief in that is among the necessities that are indispensable for belief in the Book and the Sunnah. As for knowledge beyond that of the details concerning their attributes and modalities, and detailed accounts of their reports—most of the details of their reports, attributes, and forms of their bodies have been transmitted by people through weak, objectionable, or false hadiths—there is no aspiration in the matter of creed to arrive at any of that.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents three hadiths that confirm the Quranic report about Yajuj and Majuj. First, the hadith of Zaynab bint Jahsh: the Prophet woke up alarmed, declaring that a gap had been opened in the Gog and Magog barrier, indicating that their emergence has begun. When asked if the righteous will be destroyed, he answered yes when wickedness increases. This shows that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of widespread corruption. Second, the hadith of al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an, part of a longer narration about the Dajjal and Jesus, mentions that Gog and Magog will be sent forth, and their enormous numbers will drink up Lake Tiberias. Third, the hadith of Hudhayfa ibn Asid lists ten major signs of the Hour, including Gog and Magog. The author concludes that these Quranic verses and hadiths constitute decisive evidence (dalala qati'a) that the appearance of Gog and Magog is a sign of the Hour, and belief in this is a necessary component of faith in the Book and Sunnah. Then the author adds a crucial caveat: detailed descriptions of their attributes and physical forms, which are often circulated via weak or fabricated hadiths, should not be relied upon in creedal matters ('aqida). The author thus distinguishes between what is established as necessary belief (that they will appear) and what is speculative or unreliable (specific details).

العلامات الكبرى

حديث واه
باب العقيدة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All details about Gog and Magog, such as their size, shape, and specific adventures, are part of Islamic belief.
Correction: Only the general fact of their emergence is certain from the Qur'an and authentic hadiths; most details rely on weak or fabricated narrations and are not binding in creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet woke up alarmed and said 'woe to the Arabs from an evil that has drawn near.' How much does the reality of this coming evil weigh on your heart? Do you live as if the Hour could be tomorrow, or have you become numb to these warnings? What would change if you truly believed that a gap has already been opened?
?
The author tells us that most details about Gog and Magog come from weak hadiths and are not part of creed. Yet many people confidently repeat those details. Are you careful in what you spread about the unseen, or do you pass along information without verifying its source? How can you ensure your talk about the Last Day is grounded in certainty?
?
The hadith mentions that destruction comes when wickedness increases even among the righteous. If the righteous among us today do not stand against corruption, are we already on the path to that destruction? What is one concrete way you can increase goodness in your community starting this week?

The Correct Approach to Ya'juj and Ma'juj
Author advises stopping at definitive evidence and refutes identifying them with Mongols.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct methodological approach to eschatological signs like Ya'juj and Ma'juj, and why identifying them with historical peoples is incorrect.

Core Idea
Do not speculate about unseen matters; rely only on definitive texts.

This passage from Dr. Ramadan al-Buti provides crucial guidance on how to approach the subject of Ya'juj and Ma'juj. He warns against relying on weak traditions or personal deductions, and emphasizes the need to stop at what is definitively established. He also refutes the common claim that they were the Mongols and Tatars.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the literal translation to understand the author's exact words.
Pay attention to the key terms like 'dalalah qat'iyyah' and 'rajm bil-ghayb'.
2
Identify the methodological principles
Look for the author's instructions: stop at definitive indication, wait for reality, and avoid weak traditions. These form the core advice.
3
Understand the refutation
The author rejects the identification of Ya'juj and Ma'juj with the Mongols/Tatars. Note how he uses authentic hadiths to show they appear after the Dajjal and during Jesus' descent.
This corrects a common misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخير من الخوض في ذلك أن نقف عند حدود الدلالة القطعية التي ثبتت بصريح القرآن وصحاح الأحاديث الواردة عن الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ثم تنتظر في معرفة الكنه والتفاصيل، الواقع الزمني نفسه ، فهو الذي سيتكفل وحده بشرح كل شيء عنهم . وذلك لأن يأجوج ومأجوج غيب من الغيوب التي أخبرنا الله عن ظهورهم بين يدي الساعة ، وهو أمر لم يظهر بعد ، فهو لا يزال في تلافيف الغيب لم يتبد لنا منه إلا الإخبار عنه بشكل إجمالي . إذ لا عبرة بالتفصيلات التي وصلتنا بالطرق الباطلة أو الواهية . وإذا فلا معنى للخوض في شيء لا سبيل إلى العلم بتفصيلاته اللهم إلا سبيل الرجم بالغيب ومن هنا تعلم ، أن ماقد يقوله بعضهم استنتاجاً واجتهاداً ، من أن يأجوج ومأجوج هم التتر والمغول الذين جاؤوا وانتهوا - كلام لا معتمد له ولا داعي إليه ، بل هو فيما يبدو مخالف لنصوص الأحاديث الصحيحة الدالة على أنهم إنما يظهرون في وقت نزول عيسى بن مريم وبعد ظهور الدجال . وحسبنا أن نعلم بأن هذه الأمة إذا ظهرت فإن ظهورها سيتكفل بالتعريف بها للناس كلهم تعريفاً لا يشوبه شك أو احتمال ولا يحوج إلى استنتاج أو اجتهاد .
And the best thing than delving into that is that we stop at the limits of definitive indication that has been established by the clear text of the Qur'an and the sound hadiths from the Messenger (peace and blessings be upon him), then we wait for the knowledge of the essence and details, the actual temporal reality itself, for it alone will undertake to explain everything about them. That is because Ya'juj and Ma'juj are an unseen from the unseen things that Allah informed us of their appearance before the Hour, and it is a matter that has not yet appeared, so it still remains in the folds of the unseen; nothing has become clear to us from it except the general report about it. For there is no consideration for the details that have reached us through false or weak ways. And if so, there is no meaning in delving into something for which there is no way to know its details, except the way of casting at the unseen. And from this you learn that what some people say by deduction and ijtihad, that Ya'juj and Ma'juj are the Tatars and Mongols who came and ended—it is a statement that has no reliance and no need for it; rather, it appears to contradict the texts of the authentic hadiths indicating that they only appear at the time of the descent of Jesus son of Mary and after the appearance of the Dajjal. And it is sufficient for us to know that when this nation appears, its appearance will undertake to introduce itself to all people with an introduction that is free of any doubt or probability and does not require deduction or ijtihad.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage provides methodological guidance for dealing with eschatological signs like Ya'juj and Ma'juj. The author argues that we must confine ourselves to definitive proofs from the Qur'an and sound hadith, and not engage in speculation. He explains that Ya'juj and Ma'juj are an unseen matter that has not yet occurred; therefore, details from weak sources are worthless. He then refutes the claim that they are the extinct Mongols and Tatars, noting that authentic hadiths place their appearance after the Dajjal and during the time of Jesus. Finally, he reassures that when they do appear, their identity will be unmistakable, leaving no room for doubt or interpretation.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
غيب
الدلالة القطعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ya'juj and Ma'juj were the historical Tatars and Mongols who have already come and gone.
Correction: Authentic hadiths indicate they appear after the Dajjal and during the time of Jesus (peace be upon him), so they are still future.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is it incorrect to say Ya'juj and Ma'juj were the Tatars and Mongols?
A) Because they came and went before Islam
B) Because authentic hadiths show they appear after the Dajjal and during Jesus' time
C) Because there is no mention of them in the Qur'an
D) Because they are actually a type of animal

Key Takeaway
The proper approach to eschatological signs is to rely on definitive texts and avoid speculation; false identifications like the Mongols are refuted by authentic hadiths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What unseen matter in your life—whether about the future, the afterlife, or others—do you find yourself speculating about instead of submitting to what Allah has revealed? Will you repent and stop that speculation today?
?
The author warns against 'casting at the unseen.' When have you engaged in such speculation about religious matters, perhaps about eschatological signs or other unseen events? Commit now to seek only authentic knowledge and to remain silent on what you do not know.
?
If you knew that the exact time and details of Ya'juj and Ma'juj's appearance are not for you to know, how would that change the way you spend your time and energy? Will you redirect your focus to actions that are certain and beneficial for your faith?

The Beast of the Earth: Definition and Proofs
Author defines the Beast of the Earth and provides Quranic and hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the Beast of the Earth and the Quranic and hadith evidence for its appearance as a major sign of the Hour.

Core Idea
The Beast of the Earth is a literal creature that will mark believers and disbelievers before the Hour.

The author now turns to one of the major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth (Dabbat al-Ard). He begins by defining it based on the Quran, then supports the definition with multiple authentic hadiths. Pay attention to how the author uses both primary sources to establish this as a factual event in Islamic creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the entire Arabic passage and its translation. Note the author's style: he first gives a definition, then quotes the Quranic verse, and then cites three hadiths.
The passage combines definition and evidence in one flow.
2
Understand the definition
Identify the key elements in the author's definition: the Beast is an animal whose specific nature is known only to Allah, it will appear before the Hour, speak to people, and mark each person according to their faith.
The marking (wasm) is a physical sign of faith or disbelief.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse from Surah An-Naml (27:82). Notice how it directly states that Allah will bring forth a creature from the earth that speaks to people.
The verse is the primary Quranic evidence for the Beast.
4
Analyze the three hadiths
The author quotes three hadiths from Sahih Muslim. The first establishes the Beast as one of the first signs alongside the rising sun from the west. The second lists it among six signs to hasten with deeds. The third includes it among ten signs before the Hour.
These hadiths reinforce the Beast's reality and timing.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the author presents this as a matter of 'aqidah: belief in the Beast is part of belief in the unseen. Reflect on the common misconception that it is allegorical.
The author treats it as a literal, physical event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- ظهور دابة الأرض :
ودابة الأرض تعبير قرآني عن حيوان نكل علم نوعه وشكله وهيئته إلى الله عز وجل ، يظهر للناس قبيل الساعة يكلمهم ويصف كلاً منهم بصفته من الإيمان أو الكفر ، فيَسِمُ الكافر بوسم الكفر ، ويطبع المؤمن بطابع الإيمان . وحينئذ لا تنفع نفساً إيمانها إن لم تكن قد آمنت من قبل
يقول الله عز وجل في ذلك : ﴿ وَإِذَا وَقَعَ القَوْلُ عَلَيْهِم أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُم دَابَّةٌ مِنَ الأرضِ تُكَلِّمُهُم أَنَّ النّاسَ كانوا بِآيَاتِنا لا يُوقِنُون ﴾ [النمل : ۸۲]
وروى مسلم بسنده عن عبد الله بن عمرو ، قال : حفظت من رسول الله حديثاً لم أنسه بعد ، سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : « إن أول الآيــات خروجاً طلوع الشمس من مغربها وخروج الدابة على الناس ضحى وأيتها كانت قبل صاحبتها فالأخرى على أثرها قريباً »
وروى مسلم أيضاً عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه قال : قال رسول الله بادروا بالأعمال ستة : طلوع الشمس من مغربها والدخان والدجال ، والدابة وخاصة أحدكم وأمر العامة
وروينا آنفاً عن مسلم وغيره حديث : ما تذاكرون ؟ قالوا : نذكر الساعة ، قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات وعد منها دابة الأرض
- Appearance of the Beast of the Earth:
And the Beast of the Earth is a Quranic expression for an animal whose type, form, and appearance we consign to Allah Almighty; it appears to people before the Hour, speaking to them and describing each one of them with his attribute of faith or disbelief; so it marks the disbeliever with the mark of disbelief, and stamps the believer with the stamp of faith. And then no soul's faith will benefit if it had not believed before.
Allah Almighty says concerning that: {And when the Word is fulfilled against them, We will bring forth for them a creature from the earth speaking to them, that the people were not certain of Our signs} [An-Naml: 82].
And Muslim narrated with his chain from Abdullah ibn Amr, who said: I memorized from the Messenger of Allah a hadith that I have not forgotten afterwards: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Indeed the first of the signs to appear is the rising of the sun from its west and the emergence of the Beast to the people in the forenoon; whichever of them appears first, the other follows it closely.'
And Muslim also narrated from Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Hasten with deeds before six [things]: the rising of the sun from its west, the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the death of one of you, and the general matter.'
And we have previously narrated from Muslim and others the hadith: 'What are you discussing?' They said: 'We are mentioning the Hour.' He said: 'It will not be established until you see before it ten signs,' and he counted among them the Beast of the Earth.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage defines and provides evidence for one of the major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth (Dabbat al-Ard). The author first gives its Quranic definition: a creature whose exact nature is known only to Allah, which will emerge before the Hour, speak to people, and distinguish believers from disbelievers by marking them. He then quotes the Quranic verse from Surah An-Naml. Following this, he cites three hadiths: one from Muslim about the Beast appearing alongside the rising sun from the west, another from Abu Huraira listing six signs including the Beast, and a final hadith mentioning the Beast among ten signs. These hadiths establish the Beast as a literal, future event.

Key Terms
دابة الأرض
الوسم
طابع الإيمان
قبيل الساعة
سورة النمل
